Oath-Taking Ceremony for Various Guangdong Officials: Original Text of Chairman Chiang's Address (Continued) 65

Regarding Guangdong's politics and society, we must first address the most urgent reforms and ensure the following three matters are handled first. First, eradicate corruption. Second, eliminate opium and gambling. Third, cease competing with the people for profit.

Regarding the first point, the corruption of Guangdong's past politics is something everyone has been deeply pained by. Heavy and overlapping taxes and levies provided limited gains for the government, while the people suffered endlessly. Going forward, we must encourage integrity in character, reduce burdens in politics, and use strict laws to punish corruption. We must ensure that all malpractices are eradicated, bribery disappears, and we move into a bright and progressive political system.

This point is closely related to personnel management. The reason corruption cannot be eradicated is mostly due to a lack of freedom in personnel appointments within various agencies. In revolutionary politics, there are so-called 'lucrative' and 'lean' positions, which is inherently a shameful thing. However, these lucrative positions are often filled by individuals recommended by powerful figures in the Party and military. This not only prevents the heads of departments and agencies from carrying out rectification but also gives rise to corrupt politics.

Going forward, no military officer at any level should casually recommend individuals to Party and government agencies. Furthermore, Party and government officials in charge must strictly adhere to their authority and not casually recommend individuals to agencies at the same level or subordinate agencies. The person in charge must be able to take full responsibility, after which the superiors can effectively supervise, ensuring that politics is on the right track.

For example, now that I, Chiang Kai-shek, am serving as the President of the Executive Yuan, apart from the appointments I regularly make within my jurisdiction, I have not recommended a single person to any department. I fully trust the heads of each ministry and commission to appoint personnel responsibly, following the selection regulations. However, I will supervise and penalize those who fail in their duties, ensuring that the heads of all subordinate agencies can take full responsibility without being constrained or interfered with. This is a principle that superiors must adhere to, and it is also the key to political success.

In short, we must each recognize our own authority and responsibilities and never infringe upon the authority of superiors, peers, or subordinates. Only then can we ensure that politics is clean and transparent. Know that if relatives and friends truly have the knowledge, experience, and qualifications, they will naturally have opportunities to serve even without recommendations. This is the foundation for creating a clean government, and the key is to enforce the law impartially. When encountering corruption or bribery, we must punish them to the fullest extent.

This time, the military, financial, and Party officials sent by the Central Government should especially serve as role models. If they engage in personal gain or corruption, Chiang Kai-shek will definitely take strict action and punish them according to military law. Right now, the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters will set up a tip box. If any Central Government personnel engage in personal gain or corruption, the people can submit reports. However, the informant must provide their real name and address, as well as accurate information and evidence.

In short, we must make Guangdong's military, financial, and Party affairs a model for the whole country, and we must not allow the slightest bit of favoritism.

Secondly, we must exert all our strength to eliminate opium and gambling. Opium and gambling are a stain on revolutionary politics that must be removed. The fact that opium dens and gambling houses still exist in Guangdong today is truly a disgrace to our Party. The Central Government has made a firm decision that no matter how difficult the financial situation, we will not seek a single cent of tax revenue from these harmful and destructive vices. We must strictly eliminate them. Because if opium and gambling are not eliminated, not only will society be harmed, leading to lethargy, dissipation, moral decay, and ruin, but also military discipline will be impossible to rectify. Therefore, in the future, whether it is the evaluation of political officials or military officers, we must use the thorough elimination of opium and gambling as the standard for rewards and punishments. Society should also regard it as a major enemy and strive to eradicate it. The entire Party, government, and military should treat this as a major matter. We must know that even if we cannot bring benefits to the people today, we must passively eliminate harm for the people.

Third, we must strongly avoid competing with the people for profit. In the past, Guangdong used "control" as a pretext to put many industries under the name of government operation, seeking personal gain for a few. This is absolutely unacceptable. Our revolutionary politics is about creating wealth for the people, not seizing wealth from the people, and even less about using the power of government offices to compete for profit with the people. The so-called "control" should only be limited to the necessities of national defense and economic self-defense, as well as the development of basic industries. It should not be a predatory approach like in the past that can be called "control."

Therefore, going forward, we must thoroughly review all industries to ensure that the people's interests are not infringed upon. We must ensure that the country, society, and the people all benefit and absolutely cannot deprive the people of their interests for self-enrichment. All undertakings that violate this principle should be cancelled.

Related to this is that we must pay attention to the governance of officials, carefully select officials who love the people, and evaluate them. We must ensure that commissioners and county magistrates can truly take responsibility for relieving the people's suffering.

The above three points are the most urgent matters that must be addressed first. Other matters that should be promoted or reformed in politics, Chairman Huang, being virtuous and just, will surely lead all our comrades to respond together in the Party, government, and military to carry them out earnestly, so as not to fail the expectations of the people of Guangdong.

The above explains the three important matters we must strive to do in a passive way. In addition to this, we must pay attention to the fact that revolution is about implementing the Three Principles of the People, and the spirit of the principles lies in what the Premier had repeatedly warned us, that we must restore the inherent spirit and morality of the nation in order to restore the inherent position of the nation. Therefore, we must abide by the Premier's teachings of the Eight Virtues: loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, harmony, and peace. In terms of implementation, whether in the Party, government, or military, we must start with the spirit of "propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame." The ancients said, "Propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame are the four pillars of a nation; if the four pillars are not upheld, the nation will perish." Although this is an old saying, it is truly the supreme principle for governing the country in a revolutionary way.

The so-called "propriety" is actually about procedures and discipline. "Propriety" is not only about form but also about discipline in practice. The reason China has become so disorganized, poor, weak, and vulnerable to foreign bullying and aggression is because it did not know the importance of discipline and lacked the spirit of observing the law and abiding by the rules. Therefore, the country and the nation have become disorganized. If we want to strive to be modern citizens, we must strictly abide by the discipline of the Party and the country, be able to obey on the one hand, and be responsible on the other, supporting and encouraging each other, not infringing upon or betraying each other. This is the ultimate meaning of propriety.

The so-called "righteousness" is to be selfless and impartial. Where righteousness lies, one should be willing to die for it. We have principles in the Party and justice in society. We should not shirk responsibility or be perfunctory, but only follow righteousness, not fear the strong, and not seek personal gain. Like this time, Commander Yu and the air force officers and soldiers pledged allegiance to the Central Government, which is an expression of the spirit of righteousness.

As for the so-called "integrity," it must be done thoroughly, but one must recognize one's own position and not infringe upon the authority of others. The ancients said, "Honing integrity and uprightness" means firmly adhering to strict boundaries.

The so-called "shame" is a very profound realization. Taking Guangdong as an example, opium, corruption, and prostitution are tangible shames. The ancients said, "There is no greater shame than not knowing shame." Because one does not know shame, one becomes negligent and indifferent, ultimately bringing about great shame. Extending this further, why has our revolution not succeeded to this day, and why has the country been brought to such a humiliating and painful state? All of this is the indelible shame of our Party members, officials, and military personnel. Knowing shame is the ability to act, and knowing shame is the commitment to not shirking responsibility. Therefore, our Party, government, and military comrades must wash away the stains of the past and promote future undertakings. We must lead by example and encourage ourselves with the four pillars of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame. Anything that is in accordance with propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame should be done without regard to interests, and anything that violates propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame must be avoided at all costs, even if there are swords and axes in front or benefits behind.

This time, the revolutionary soldiers of Guangdong have revived the revolutionary spirit. The question now is how to seize this promising opportunity, promote the existing glory, and complete the revolutionary cause. To achieve this goal, we must first establish Party, government, and military agencies with principles, responsibility, and discipline. First and foremost, our Party, government, and military comrades must eliminate the decadent habits of arrogance, extravagance, indulgence, romance, and corruption, and promote the upright spirit of hard work, endurance, simplicity, and perseverance. In short, we must establish an independent, unwavering, and flawless personality, lead by example, and transform the atmosphere, inspiring people's hearts. Not only must we thoroughly reform our past bad habits, thoughts, and actions, but we must also make our revolutionary army a model for the people, make our Party headquarters a center of revolution, and make our government a clean and capable government. All personnel in upper and lower agencies should develop a strict and upright style, not only treating subordinates with strictness, but also treating themselves with greater strictness, not only disciplining others with righteousness, but especially disciplining themselves with righteousness. Only in this way can we shoulder the important responsibilities of the revolution and accomplish our common mission.

I hope everyone will encourage each other and supervise each other. If the central authorities have actions that are unjust or not strict, any comrade should first punish them according to Party discipline and national law. If Chiang Kai-shek violates revolutionary principles, any compatriot and subordinate can treat me as a rebel.

Why do we emphasize the words "discipline" and "uprightness" again to encourage our comrades? Know that our country is in the midst of an unprecedented national crisis, and our revolution is at a critical juncture of success or failure. Everyone must not be careless or slack in the slightest, otherwise the nation will never recover and the country will not be able to exist.

Coming to today's grand meeting, we cannot help but think of the past. The various changes in Guangdong in the past were not actually due to the inherent nature of the troublemakers. As I said above, I personally cannot but take the blame. The biggest reason is that I did not tell them about the great righteousness and the right path of the revolution in a very strict manner, nor could I supervise them with a strict attitude. Therefore, some people say that Guangdong has been chaotic for years because of the Central Government's excessive indulgence. Because of being accustomed to indulgence, over time, bad habits gradually developed, and in the end, they became almost incurable, not only harming the local area and the country, but also harming the subordinates in practice. I thought that those who were responsible for Guangdong in the past, such as Li Renzhao, Chen Zhenru, and even Chen Bonan, if they had adhered to Party and national discipline and followed the right path in everything, how could they not have made great contributions to the country and the revolution? It was only because Chiang Kai-shek's sincerity was not trusted and the Central Government was too indulgent that they misled the country and themselves. It is really painful. This is not only their fault, but also Chiang Kai-shek's fault. Today, returning to Guangzhou, reflecting on the present and thinking about the past, I am really ashamed and guilty. Therefore, today I petition the Central Government to pardon Li, Chen, and their affiliated subordinates, and I want to request punishment myself.

In the future, if we want our comrades to succeed in their careers, we must love people with virtue and expect them to be strict and upright. Know that there is a difference between strictness and harshness, and there is also a difference between interfering with actions and restricting actions, and there is even more of a difference between restricting freedom and depriving freedom. If our comrades have improper places, interfering with him and correcting him is precisely to perfect him. Regarding the highest interests of the Party and the country, and what is not allowed in the rules and regulations, our restrictions on him are actually protecting him. A soldier, official, and Party member has no freedom, only the country has freedom. The Premier's precious teachings are indeed an unchanging rule for all ages. If there is no restriction for one day, there will be indulgence every day, and in the end, they will go on a dangerous path and lose their protection. If one place is not interfered with, then every place will be out of bounds, and it will inevitably fail to complete its beginning and end. Going out of bounds and indulging for a long time can create a step towards doing evil. Therefore, our Party, government, and military comrades, in order to maintain a consistent history and cause from top to bottom, must strictly abide by discipline and be wary at all times, and at the same time must do their best to fulfill their duties, and must not fail to advise when there is wrongdoing, and must not fail to encourage when there is goodness. Especially those responsible comrades who are in the position of supporting the career of superiors, and have the responsibility of the success or failure of the career, should thoroughly understand this meaning. A gentleman loves people with virtue, so he should take principles and morality as the standard for both superiors and subordinates, and should not be eager for immediate success and petty gains, so as to confuse the upper and lower levels and lose the revolutionary stance. Since we are a common body of life and death, we should regard honor and disgrace and praise and slander as one. At this time of re-establishing the foundation, in order to expect the revolution and everyone's success in their careers, I have specially put it forward and earnestly told you, I believe that our comrades in the field, both civil and military, will definitely accept this heartfelt advice, especially be careful to the end. There is still one very important meaning to say, that is, the relationship between Guangdong and the Central Government, whether in the East or in China, will rise from Guangdong, and in the future, it must also rely on the strength of Guangdong to achieve the final success. This is Guangdong's unique responsibility, and it is also Guangdong's unique honor. The contribution of the people of Guangdong to the country and the revolution is shining for all ages. Also because of this, Guangdong and the Central Government must not have any separation. Know that without Guangdong, there would be no Central Government today, and without the Central Government, there would be no Guangdong today. Therefore, if the Central Government is strong and stable, it is Guangdong's welfare. Conversely, if the Central Government fails, it is Guangdong's failure, and it is the failure of the entire revolution. Guangdong and the Central Government share the same honor and disgrace, interests and losses, and are completely one. Although today's Central Government is in Nanjing, its spirit is completely in Guangdong. In terms of Party affairs, the number of Party members in Guangdong exceeds that of any province, so the task of Guangdong comrades is particularly important, and they must especially cherish and love themselves, continue the spirit left by the Premier, and complete the final task of the revolution. The Central Government cannot do without Guangdong, and if Guangdong leaves the Central Government, it will inevitably fall into failure and pain. If the Central Government succeeds, Guangdong will also succeed. In the past, the Guangdong authorities did not know this meaning. People like Li Renzhao, Chen Zhenru, and Chen Bonan thought that without the Central Government, Guangdong could also exist, and without the Central Government leading the Guangdong army, it could also exist independently. This is a big mistake. Know that the whole revolution lies in the consolidation of the foundation, and the Central Government is the foundation for consolidating the revolution. If there are only limbs and no head, then its spirit will have nowhere to be entrusted, and how can it exist? Therefore, the Central Government and Guangdong cannot be separated, and Chiang Kai-shek, Director Yu, Chairman Huang, and the comrades of the land, sea, and air forces in Guangdong are also the same, and cannot be separated. In the future, there must not be any distinction between each other. The general compatriots and comrades in Guangdong, as well as the military, must know this meaning. If Guangdong is unified, of course the strength of the Central Government will increase, but it must be known that this is the basic stability of the revolution, and it is actually the increase in Guangdong's welfare. Whether it is to people, to things, or to economic relations, in the future, there must be no distinction between the Central Government and the local government. In other provinces, it may be regarded that there is a distinction between the Central Government and the local government, but in Guangdong, the Central Government and the local government are completely one. If everyone thoroughly recognizes this point, the glory of Guangdong's future will be limitless, and the future of the Chinese revolution will also be limitless. In short, this time it can be said that not only has the revolutionary base been restored, but also the revolutionary spirit of our Party has been restored. From this, I am reminded of the past, in the painful environment of the past, many revolutionary comrades have suffered oppression and tasted sacrifices, and it is even more worthy of our remembrance that they have maintained a line of righteousness. Since there is such a glorious and great achievement this time, everyone must know that such an achievement is very difficult to obtain and easy to lose, and they must be cautious and fearful and do their best to maintain it, reversing their previous actions, thoughts, and habits, and thoroughly understanding what Guangdong's position is and what its responsibilities are. Especially the Guangdong soldiers must recognize their own responsibilities and position, and know the difficulty of creating a new situation, and jointly maintain the existing cause, and strive to promote it, so that Guangdong can fulfill its greatest responsibility in the future revolutionary history. I hope that our Party, government, and military officials in charge, from today onwards, will especially unite sincerely, work together harmoniously, endure hardship and hard work, and work together to cultivate the great personality of revolutionaries for themselves, and build Guangdong into a model province and region, create a healthy Party headquarters, establish a clean government, in order to consolidate our revolutionary base and restore the glory of our Party's revolutionary history. Only in this way can we be worthy of the compatriots of the whole province of Guangdong, not fail the expectations of the people of the whole country, and also comfort the spirit of our Premier in heaven. (The End)

Anhui Province: High-Profile Adjustment of Mobile Finance; Issuance of Subsidiary Coin Notes Worth 2.5 Million Yuan; Clearing of Private Notes with Denominations of One, Two, and Five Jiao 66

Wuhu Correspondence: Although Anhui Province is adjacent to the Yangtze River, its customs are closed and conservative. In terms of finance, what the people trust the most are only hard coins, namely "Large Dragon Dollars" and "Small Copper Coins." Paper money only circulates among large shops and intellectuals. This is because Anhui Province is essentially an agricultural area. Wuhu is the only port for foreign trade, and there is virtually no industry. Rural farmers have simple minds and are easily prejudiced. Regarding the use of paper money, they are often suspicious and worried, which causes frequent obstacles to financial adjustment. In particular, the leakage and loss of copper coins make them increasingly scarce and difficult to circulate. Local public organizations or shops in various counties of northern Anhui take the opportunity to issue jiao notes and cash notes without authorization. The reserve funds are unverifiable, and the exchange rate is without any standard, leading to numerous malpractices. Although the people suffer from it, there is nothing they can do. In recent years, although the subsidiary coin notes of the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Central Bank, and the Farmers Bank can be widely used throughout the province, the amount is still insufficient to meet the demand. Profiteers often require premiums for exchange. The various hard subsidiary coins newly issued by the Central Government are extremely limited in their inflow into Anhui Province, serving only for people to collect and admire. The scarcity of copper coins and the shortage of subsidiary coins have invisibly raised the prices of daily necessities, which has a significant impact on people's livelihoods. The Anhui Provincial Government, after much assessment, believes that there is an urgent need to seek relief. Therefore, it intends to comply with Article 10 of the "Provisional Measures for Provincial Banks or Local Banks to Obtain or Issue Convertible Notes" approved by the Central Political Conference, and Anhui has a local bank to issue subsidiary coin notes worth 5 million yuan, so that finance in various places can be unblocked, and the illegal issuance of notes can also be rectified and cleared. After consulting the Ministry of Finance, it was approved to issue 2.5 million yuan because the amount was too large, and ordered to properly allocate the types and amounts of the subsidiary coin notes to be ordered and printed, and report to the ministry for approval. At the same time, it still follows the regulations to deposit cash and guarantee reserves with the local Central Bank for safekeeping. When the amount of new subsidiary coins issued by the Central Government is sufficient to meet the needs, the subsidiary coin notes of the Anhui Bank may be ordered to be withdrawn at any time to unify the monetary policy. After receiving this reply from the Ministry of Finance, the provincial government immediately ordered the local bank to actively prepare. It has now been determined that the subsidiary coin notes will be divided into three types: one jiao, two jiao, and five jiao. The design has already been drawn, and it has been decided to use the Zhenfeng Pagoda of Yingjiang Temple in Anqing as the symbol. It is estimated that within two months, these subsidiary coin notes will be circulating in various places in Anhui Province. (18th)

Hubei Agricultural Cooperation Undertaking: Loans of Nearly 2 Million Yuan; Promotion of Eastern Hubei Social Affairs; Establishment of a Cooperative Treasury 67

Hankou Correspondence: The Hubei Provincial Rural Cooperation Committee has been established for more than two years, and it has made great efforts to provide financial relief to rural areas in various counties. This year, Hubei Province has had a bumper harvest of agricultural products, and the rural situation has slightly improved. The committee has formulated specific plans for the future development of cooperative undertakings. According to the person in charge of the committee, "This committee was established two years ago in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters, and the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters designated responsible personnel to organize the Rural Cooperation Committee. Jia Shiyi, the Director of the Finance Department, was specially responsible for handling it and achieved considerable results. Finally, Jia resigned from his concurrent post due to busy affairs, and the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters reassigned Liu Shoupeng, the Director of the Construction Department, to take over as the Chairman of the committee and ordered the Farmers Bank to coordinate the loans to serve as the foundation for establishing rural cooperatives in various counties. Currently, the cooperatives established by this committee include ten counties: Huanggang, Xiaogan, Xishui, Yingshan, Yunmeng, Anlu, Xianning, Jiayu, Suixian, and Zaoyang. The sixteen pre-cooperatives hosted by the former Rural Financial Relief Office (Yangxin, Chongyang, Echeng, Daye, Tongshan, Tongcheng, Mianyang, Jianli, Qianjiang, Enshi, Hefeng, Huang'an, Lishan, Macheng, Yingshan, Luotian, etc.), and the eight cooperative societies of Wuchang, Hanyang, Hankou, Huangpi, Huangmei, Yichang, Hanchuan, Jiangling (loans by Huayang Yizhenhui and managed by The Farmers Bank of China) have all been transferred to the committee. The sum is 37 counties. As of the end of June, a comparison of the foreign currencies loaned by the cooperatives of the 37 counties with the foreign currencies returned shows that one-third of the loans has been repaid. This year, the agricultural products of various counties are very abundant, and the repayments should be even more enthusiastic, which is very beneficial to the social, economic, and economic life of the people. The Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters, in view of the fact that the Hubei border area has been plagued by red bandits and continuous droughts for many years, has specially ordered the committee to send personnel to guide and promote the social affairs of eastern Hubei and establish a cooperative treasury. It has now achieved considerable development. In the future, it is planned to establish offices in the county division areas, and the cooperative administration will be handled by the affiliated district offices in charge, so as to realize the practical effect of cooperation." (August 16)

Wuxi: Police Unrest Resolved Satisfactorily 72

Zhang Da, the Director of the Public Security Bureau of this county, due to the reorganization of the police administration district system, transferred 184 police officers from the original branch chiefs and police officers to the province for training. The police officers, unwilling to go to the province, petitioned the county bureau, requesting the issuance of gratuities for dismissal. At that time, there were no results, which led to a city-wide strike. Local security was maintained by security team members and student police officers sent by the province. Details of the process have been recorded in this newspaper. Now, it is known that County Magistrate Long Tiyao has repeatedly summoned the police officers to speak with them. On the night before last, at about 10 o'clock, he sent eleven county government officials to divide all the police officers into eleven groups, and talked to them individually in the Wenxi Hall, asking if they were willing to be transferred to other counties by the province. As a result, 67 people were willing to go to the province and be transferred to other counties, and 55 people were unwilling to go to the province. Yesterday (the 19th), in the early morning, the general bureau assigned 150 student police officers to serve in various branches, with 30 to the first branch, 40 to the fifth branch, 30 to the fourth branch, and 50 to the third branch, all stationed on the roads and main thoroughfares. Thus, the strike was satisfactorily resolved.

Jiaxing: Apprentice Falls to His Death 78

Li Ashou, an apprentice at Xia Taifeng Leather Goods Store at Zhong'an Bridge in Jiaxing North Street (from Shaoxing, 20 years old), went to the window to dry clothes at noon on the 17th. He stepped on a wooden strip erected by the window, which broke under the weight. He fell to the stone road of Zhong'an Bridge, fainting on the spot, with blood gushing from his mouth and ears. The situation was very tragic. He was sent to Fuyin Hospital for treatment. Although there were no external injuries, his brain, waist, and internal organs were severely shaken. The injury was extremely severe. By the evening, his fever rose and he fell into a coma. When the store owner brought his mother (a domestic servant in Hangzhou), he was unable to speak. He died on the 18th. The store owner prepared a coffin and had him encoffined, and his mother transported the coffin back to Shao'an for burial.

Bengbu: Tongji Pharmacy Sealed Off 80

Personnel from the Supervision Department of the Bengbu Public Security Bureau recently led detectives to the Tongji Pharmacy on the main street of the city, where they seized a large number of highly toxic drugs and four wanted criminals: Zhang Huiqun (female), Xing Fengxiang, Zhang Hanjun, and Zhang Fashu. They were immediately taken to the bureau and detained. The authorities, considering the Tongji Pharmacy as the main organ for trafficking drugs, paid special attention to it. At that time, detectives were sent to investigate near the pharmacy. Suspects Shen Kaiwen and Hu Furen, who went to the pharmacy to visit, were also captured and taken to the bureau for custody. Director Lu Zongjing, considering the case to be serious, telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Government and the Fourth District Commissioner's Office separately. Subsequently, he requested medical experts to chemically test the seized four packages of drugs, which were proven to be a mixture of morphine essence and caffeine essence, a highly addictive narcotic drug that has long been strictly prohibited from trafficking. These sixty-six large packages of drugs weighed a total of 159 jin. At 7 a.m. on the 17th, detectives from the Supervision Department of the Public Security Bureau searched the pharmacy again, but found nothing. The police were dispatched to seal the pharmacy's gate, and the pharmacy's business was suspended. At about 9 a.m., the director sent Inspector Zou Zhensheng, leading 16 police officers, to escort the six male and female criminals, Zhang Huiqun, Xing Hongxiang, Zhang Hanchen, Zhang Fashu, Shen Kaiwen, and Hu Furen, along with the drug evidence, on the Changhuai small steamer to the Huaiyuan County Government, where they were handed over to the County Magistrate and Military Judge for interrogation according to the law.

Citizen Registration Completed, Swearing-in Date and Location to Be Announced Separately, Supplementary Swearing-in for Group Staff Today 81

The citizen registration for general citizens in this city, which started the day before yesterday, ended yesterday. The office still dispatched a large number of personnel to collect the forms door-to-door throughout the city's streets and alleys. The total number of registration forms issued the day before yesterday is still difficult to count, but it is estimated to be more than two million. From today, they will be sorted and organized according to streets, lanes, and neighborhoods. As for the date and location of the swearing-in, it will be determined after the registration forms are sorted, based on the number of people in each area, the distribution of residences, and the convenience of their occupations, and will be announced separately.

Supplementary Swearing-in for Groups: The citizen registration and swearing-in for staff of various professional groups and freelance professional groups have already been held. The National Election Office, fearing that there may still be omissions, has arranged for supplementary swearing-in in three locations throughout the day today. The first location is the General Labor Union, where all cadres, councilors, and labor union directors and supervisors of the various district farmers' associations and fishermen's associations who have not yet been sworn in will go to complete the procedure. The second location is the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, where all executive and supervisory committee members of the various trade associations who have not been sworn in will go to complete the procedure. The third location is the Municipal Education Association, where all members of the Accountants' Association, Journalists' Association, Physicians' Association, and various district education associations who have not been sworn in will go to complete the procedure.

Citizen Certificates Being Rushed into Production: Regarding the staff and members of various agencies and groups who have completed the citizen swearing-in registration procedures, citizen certificates must be issued in accordance with the law based on the oath registration forms, so that they can receive election tickets and enjoy civil rights in the future. The number of these citizen certificates is extremely large. The National Election Office has fully mobilized since the day before yesterday to work on this matter. After the completion of the filling, it can be announced for distribution. In addition, the preliminary elections for various professional groups and freelance professional groups (i.e., the executive organ staff of lower-level groups select candidates) will also begin according to the election procedures. Therefore, the internal work of the office has been extremely tense in recent days.

Qualifications of Group Members: The National Election Office received instructions from the General Office yesterday regarding the qualifications of group members to participate in elections. The original order stated that according to the request for interpretation of Article 19 of the Election Law, "The professional groups and freelance professional groups participating in the election shall be limited to those established in accordance with the law before the promulgation of this law." Whether the qualifications of new members are also limited to those legally determined before the promulgation of the Election Law are included in the meaning, according to this, after investigation, Article 19 of the Election Law has clearly stipulated that professional and freelance professional groups are limited to those established in accordance with the law before the promulgation of this law, then the qualifications of members who organize the groups and have the right to vote, in order to implement the legislative spirit of this article, should also be limited to those legally obtained before the promulgation of the Election Law, etc. The office has already notified and complied with this.

Supplementary Swearing-in for Journalists: The citizen registration and swearing-in of the Journalists' Association of this city was held on the 17th of this month at the association's headquarters. However, there are still many who were unable to participate due to circumstances. The association has now received a notice from the National Election Office that those who have not participated in registration and swearing-in on the prescribed date will be registered and sworn in throughout the day today (the 20th) at the Municipal Education Association at the South City Public Stadium. The National Election Office has appointed Tong Xingbai as the supervisor. The association, considering the matter to be related to citizens' rights and interests, has immediately notified all members who have not been sworn in. It is hoped that members who have not been sworn in will actively participate and not lightly give up their citizenship qualifications.

Finished Taxed Foreign Goods are Broken Up Into Smaller Units, Methods of Transportation and Sales, Two Railway Administrations Receive Orders from the Ministry 85

The Ministry of Railways instructed the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, "According to the Ministry of Finance, according to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's presentation, the Western Paint Industry Association sent a letter regarding how to handle the re-packaging of taxed goods into smaller units for transportation and sales in various places. Please stipulate methods so that goods transferred from Shanghai to the interior can circulate legally. It is now stipulated that for taxed foreign goods that are to be transported in batches from the original port of import to various places, or sold to retail merchants and then transported to various places, in addition to handling according to Article 1 of the transportation and sales regulations, the quantity, mark number, packaging situation, departure date, destination, etc. of the re-packaged goods, or goods that have been re-processed and then resold to various places, shall be reported to the customs with the original import tax payment certificate before shipment, and the customs will issue a transportation and sales license. The customs may investigate whether there are any abuses in the substitution of goods when necessary. If any fraudulent behavior is found, it will be punished severely in accordance with the regulations. In addition to distribution, we should consult for verification and compliance, etc." The bureau has ordered the transportation department to comply.

The Mint Increases the Casting of Subsidiary Coins, More Than 10 Million Yuan in Circulation in the Market, 30 Million Yuan Can Be Cast by the End of the Year 86

According to the Dagong News Agency, the Central Mint was ordered by the Ministry of Finance in March of this year to start casting new copper-nickel subsidiary coins. After the first batch was cast, it was inspected and qualified before being released from the factory and circulated in Beijing, Shanghai, and other places. Due to the high demand in the market, the supply could not meet the demand. The factory has been working day and night to catch up with the casting. To date, more than 10 million yuan of subsidiary coins have been cast. However, with the unification of the currency system in various places and the sharp increase in the number of subsidiary coins needed, the number already cast is still insufficient. In order to adjust the currency system and finance and complete the legal tender policy, the Ministry of Finance has ordered the factory to continue casting a large number of subsidiary coins. Therefore, even in the hot summer, the factory has not stopped work. It is estimated that by the end of this year, the number of new subsidiary coins cast will reach 30 million yuan. It is reported that the current batch of subsidiary coins being cast by the factory will be shipped to Guangdong for circulation after being collected and delivered to the Central Bank upon release from the factory.

Marshall, Chairman of the British Chamber of Commerce, Talks About Income Tax, Denies British Residents Affirmative Approval 87

According to the Zi Lin Newspaper, a Chinese newspaper reported a piece about Mr. Marshall, Chairman of the Shanghai British Chamber of Commerce, in which he said that British residents in China do not oppose the Chinese authorities collecting income tax from them. This newspaper inquired with Mr. Marshall about the truth of this statement. Mr. Marshall directly and firmly denied this statement. A reporter from a certain Chinese newspaper asked Mr. Marshall to answer certain questions regarding income tax. During the conversation, Mr. Marshall denied that British residents had made any organized opposition to this tax, because they had not considered that under the current circumstances, this tax could be applied to British residents. Mr. Marshall admitted that in theory, the principle of income tax is very sound, but everything depends on how it is implemented. The most important condition is the ability to seriously collect this tax nationwide. Taxing only people's salaries is not taxing their income. He then mentioned the establishment of a bureau to discuss such matters. Mr. Marshall replied that such an agency cannot be established overnight, and requires careful organization. For example, if the people of Jiangsu pay this tax, while the people of Sichuan are exempt, it would be unfair to the people of Jiangsu, because this tax is national in nature. Moreover, this tax is for the central government, not for the provincial government. Mr. Marshall stated that what he said did not affirm that British residents approve of this tax.

Shanghai County Deed Tax Permanently Reduced, Approximately 220,000 to 30,000 Yuan Last Year 89

The Shanghai County field and house deed tax, which was approximately 220,000 to 30,000 yuan last year, was previously ordered by the Finance Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government to reduce the tax to 6.3% for sales and 3% for mortgages (originally 9.6% for sales), and repeatedly extended the deadline. The deadline expired again at the end of last month. Now the county government has received an order from the province, which states that the deed tax rate should be set as a permanent tax rate with a maximum limit of 6.3% for sales, in order to reduce the people's burden. The short-price and concealed tax penalties originally stipulated in the deed tax regulations of this province have been revised separately, and the regulations have been issued for compliance. After receiving the order, the county government, in addition to publicly announcing it, has instructed the township heads to comply and inform the people at any time to quickly complete the taxation of untaxed white deeds in order to consolidate property rights. Since the tax reduction, the people have been very enthusiastic about completing the tax payment. According to the sales deed price paid last year, there were approximately 220,000 to 30,000 yuan. It is also reported that after the tax reduction, all deed taxes and county taxes are allowed to retain one yuan within the sale deed tax of six yuan to offset education and public security expenses. The original surcharges may not exceed half of the regular tax.

Shanghai Municipality Plans to Establish a Factory Inspection Office, Municipal Government Orders the Social Affairs Bureau to Comply 91

The Chamber of Commerce Inquires with the Zhoucun Chamber of Commerce About Artificial Silk Fabric Conditions 92

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Zhoucun Chamber of Commerce yesterday stating, "Dear Sirs, on the 18th of this month, according to a letter from the Municipal Electric Machinery Silk Weaving Industry Association, members recently reported that Minghua Ge and Zhongshan Di from Zhoucun, Shandong, have recently been found in the Shanghai silk market in increasing numbers, and five to six thousand bolts are shipped to Shanghai every day, continuously being transported without end. After investigating their wholesale prices in Shanghai, Zhongshan Di (a fabric interwoven with rayon and cotton yarn) is priced at 3.3 yuan per 2.5 pounds, and Minghua Ge (a rayon fabric) is priced at 4 yuan per 3 pounds. These prices are vastly different from the selling prices of products from domestic silk factories in Shanghai. According to the Shanghai Di of the same type as Zhongshan Di, the cost of raw materials for every 2.5 pounds is at least 3.6 yuan. For products of the same type as Minghua Ge, the tax that should be paid for every 3 pounds of rayon is 4.2 yuan. However, their selling prices are not enough to cover the cost of raw materials in one case, and lower than the tax cost in the other. The source and reason for this dumping are truly surprising and must be investigated. The government's anti-smuggling efforts have been extremely strict recently, and the inspection of the rayon used in bolt fabrics is even stricter. However, it is extremely difficult to dissect and record the raw materials for each bolt of already woven fabric. Therefore, for finished products, it can only be allowed to be sold. However, with five to six thousand bolts of Zhongshan Di and Minghua Ge from Zhoucun being shipped to Shanghai every day by mail parcels, the rayon contained in those five to six thousand bolts is approximately seven to eight thousand boxes. How many boxes of rayon are currently in stock in Zhoucun? How many bolts of finished products are there? What is the cost of rayon? It is urgent to investigate the prices. The Zhoucun Chamber of Commerce should also sympathize with the anti-smuggling work. I hereby earnestly request your association to quickly forward this letter to the Zhoucun Chamber of Commerce, requesting them to investigate the types of raw materials, selling prices, costs, inventory quantities, tax payment situations, and whether they are complying with the regulations of the Ministry of Finance regarding the inspection of imported goods and the temporary regulations for transportation and sales, and the regulations for the inspection of rayon and local product bolt fabrics, issuing licenses, reporting to customs, and handling transportation and sales for the Zhongshan Di and Minghua Ge that are shipped to Shanghai every day without end, and to reply one by one in order to clarify the source and reason for their dumping. The matter concerns the inspection and investigation of the silk weaving industry, and I dare to ask for your investigation and handling, and please reply. Enclosed are two fabric samples and a dissection report." After investigating the raw materials required for rayon fabrics, they are all purchased from foreign countries, with tariffs and freight charges added. The costs required by your weaving factories should not be lighter than those of Shanghai factories. Why are the products shipped from your area to Shanghai for sale cheaper than the goods produced by local Shanghai factories? The weaving factories in Shanghai are suspicious of this situation. The factories are all run by Chinese, and they should have the friendship of caring for each other in difficult times. Therefore, I have enclosed a fabric sample and asked your association to investigate and clarify the situation as described in the original letter and to reply quickly in order to dispel doubts and maintain the business of the Shanghai factories.

The Completion of the Ba Mao Floodgate Construction Project in Changshu: Costing 300,000 Yuan 93

According to the Shenshi News Agency, the Ba Mao River in Changshu is a crucial waterway connecting the Yangtze River and Tai Lake. It is of utmost importance for water conservation. The Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission, with the approval of the National Economic Council, allocated funds to construct the Ba Mao Mouth Floodgate to regulate the water flow appropriately. In January of this year, Kong Xiangxi, Standing Committee Member of the Economic Council and Minister of Finance, personally laid the foundation, after which construction began immediately. After more than seven months, the entire project is nearly complete. The floodgate is constructed entirely of reinforced concrete, with a height sufficient to withstand the highest tides of the Yangtze River. The height of the gate sill is 1.5 meters below the zero point of the Wusong sea level. The gate has five openings, and the gate body is 44 meters long. A bridge is built on the gate surface for the passage of cargo trucks with a load capacity of 2.5 tons. The gate is suspended and operated by hand-cranked machinery for opening and closing. The total construction cost is 300,000 yuan. According to information from the Shanghai office of the Economic Council, the floodgate project is now complete, and the council has sent personnel to Changshu for acceptance inspection. Whether or not a completion ceremony will be held has not yet been decided.

The Japanese Naval Landing Force in Shanghai Installs Military Telephones, Extending Along Doushan Road to the Suzhou Creek; Radio Stations Are Also Being Set Up in Financial Institutions 94

According to the Huadong News Agency, the Japanese Naval Landing Force in Shanghai has recently seemed very concerned with military equipment. Personnel Detained in the Sorghum Wine Industry Are Released; Full Business Resumption Begins Today; Confiscated Wine Sent to the Bureau of Commodity Inspection for Examination; Punishment Will Be Imposed According to Regulations if Alcohol is Found to Have Been Used as an Adulterant 95

Following the detention of personnel and goods from forty-two sorghum wine merchants, including Tongxinchang, by the Shanghai Inspection Office of the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Anhui District Consolidated Tax Bureau, and the subsequent suspension of business operations starting the day before yesterday, a bail arrangement was agreed upon yesterday morning. Personnel detained from Tongchangfu and Tonghe Yong wine merchants were released on bail, and full business resumption was approved starting this morning. The details are as follows:

Suspension of Business and Transportation

After the Sorghum Wine Trade Association decided to suspend business and petition, representatives He Xiansheng and others negotiated with Section Chief Jiang of the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Anhui District Consolidated Tax Bureau and Section Chief Xia of the Shanghai Inspection Office and agreed that Lai Afang and Wang Ancai of Tongchangfu Wine Merchant, and Shi Agou and others from Tonghe Yong Wine Merchant would be released on bail. The bail procedures were processed the night before last, but because the Shanghai Inspection Office noted on the bail bond "private transportation of firewater adulterated with local sorghum wine," the wine merchants expressed opposition, which led to failure to release the detained individuals. The Association originally planned to resume business after the release of those detained from Tongchangfu and others, and immediately issue a notice to resume business. Because the detained personnel were not released yesterday morning, wholesale transactions remained suspended. As for the local sorghum wine transported to Shanghai from various parts of Jiangbei, transport was also uniformly stopped from yesterday morning. The wine loaded on the new local sorghum wine boats at the Shanbochang Bridge also stopped transporting. However, the retail departments of the various wine merchants maintained normal operations. But the operation of the wine merchants mainly relies on wholesale.

Release on Bail

Yesterday morning at 10 am, the Association representative, He Xiang, again contacted Section Chief Xia of the Shanghai Inspection Office and agreed on a flexible bail arrangement. The bail procedures were then immediately processed. Lai Afang and others of Tongchangfu Wine Merchant were released on business bond at around 11 am. Shi Agou, who was detained with a wine boat from Tonghe Yong Wine Merchant, was also released on business bond at 5 p.m. yesterday. As for the confiscated wine, it was decided that the Shanghai Inspection Office would hand it over to the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Anhui District Consolidated Tax Bureau for forwarding to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau for verification. If the verification clearly showed that it was alcohol adulterated with sorghum wine, punishment would be imposed in accordance with regulations. If no alcohol adulteration was found, it would be released immediately.

Resumption of Business This Morning

A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency interviewed He Xiang, a member of the Association yesterday. According to him, the suspension of the local sorghum wine industry was due to the lack of knowledge of wine and personal integrity of the inspectors used by the Shanghai Inspection Office. Upon seeing a wine load, they considered the case to be in hand. Even the sub-director does not know good from bad wines, forcing businesses to first acknowledge and guarantee the use of alcohol as an adulterant. If the wine merchants did not provide this guarantee, the warehouse staff would be detained. They would be detained at the Shanghai Inspection Office during the day and sent to the police station at night until the Consolidated Tax Bureau completed its inspection, which could take one or two months. How could such administration not be heartbreaking? Therefore, as a last resort, we were publicly elected to petition the Consolidated Tax Bureau. The responsible section chief received us. The purpose of our petition was that the wine carriers are only responsible for delivering the wine. Since the wine has an owner, the staff should not be detained to avoid the innocent suffering. Merchants have reported to the inspection office for inspection and labeling. Re-bottled wines should not be detained midway. The two section chiefs approved our requests. Regarding the guarantee, they provided a guarantee to be summoned as needed. The detained warehouse staff from Tongchangfu were released at 11 a.m. The wine of Tonghe Yong, which had been detained for over ten days, was relocated by the inspection office. The detained wine and staff were released at 5 p.m. It was decided that business operations would be resumed starting on the 20th. The details of the bail application will be reported at a general meeting of the members.

Handling Measures

A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency visited Section Chief Jiang of the Consolidated Tax Bureau again yesterday morning. According to him, the dispute in the local sorghum wine industry has been resolved in consultation with the Association representative, He Xiang, and others. Detained personnel were released on bail by the wine merchants. As for the confiscated goods, they would be handed over to the Commodity Inspection Bureau for verification. If no alcohol adulteration was found, the goods would be released immediately. If alcohol adulteration was found, the punishment would be imposed according to regulations. Article 2 of the punitive measures for adulterating local wine with firewater states that "Wholesalers who use large quantities of ordinary firewater to adulterate local wine for wholesale business shall be fined between 200 and 1,000 yuan." Article 3 states that "Retail shops that use firewater to adulterate local wine for retail sales shall be fined between 10 and 200 yuan." Article 4 states that "In addition to the penalties prescribed in Articles 2 and 3 of these rules, the seized goods shall be confiscated."

According to the Central News Agency, the Shanghai local sorghum wine industry, because of the Shanghai Inspection Office of the Suzhou-Anhui District Consolidated Tax Bureau inspectors, forcefully claimed alcohol was illegally used as an adulterant and made detentions. After the trade association’s resolution, businesses were temporarily suspended and representatives were sent to the tax bureau to submit petitions, as reported earlier. It is now discovered that the trade association dispatched representatives from Lao Heng Xing, Tongchangfu, Tongxinchang, Dafuyong, and eight other wine merchants to the tax bureau yesterday afternoon to submit petitions. Director Sheng of the bureau dispatched Section Chiefs Jiang and Qian to receive them. After each of the representatives detailed the petition, Section Chiefs Jiang and Qian reported to Director Sheng, who earnestly persuaded and stated that the bureau aims to benefit the country and convenience merchants. If illegal detentions, obstruction, extortions, and other matters involving the inspectors should occur in the future, the wine merchants are permitted to file factual charges, and the bureau will investigate and deal with the matter strictly according to law, without leniency. However, since firewater is more than twice as cheap as local wine, unscrupulous merchants use it as an adulterant, which greatly affects tax revenue. Earlier, the Ministry of Finance issued strict orders prohibiting the adulteration of beverages. To implement the ban and safeguard the livelihood of the brewers, future cases of adulteration will be punished in accordance with the regulations to maintain tax revenue. Each of the representatives happily dispersed because Director Sheng eradicated abuses, upheld fair business practices, and spared no effort.

Blasting of Submerged Rocks in Dalian Bay: Red Flags Indicate Dangerous Areas; All Vessels Must Proceed with Caution 96

The Autumn Flood of the Huangpu River; High Tides Are Stable; Water Levels Are Below Predictions; Shipping and Storage Companies Urge Removal of Stored Goods 107

According to the Huangpu River Conservancy Bureau, the highest point of the autumn flood tide of the Huangpu River this month was predicted to be midnight the day before yesterday. According to measurements, the quantity was 12 feet 8 inches. This morning, it was learned from the bureau that fortunately, it did not reach the predicted level. The water level was below the prediction. However, there will be high tides next month. The shipping and storage companies have been urging the removal of stored goods to prevent water damage. The details are as follows:

Did Not Exceed Predictions

Because it is currently the autumn flood season, the tides of the Huangpu River are particularly high. According to the Huangpu River Conservancy Bureau's prediction, the tide on the night of the 18th (the day before yesterday) would be the highest, with a quantity of 12 feet 8 inches (the height of the bund embankment is only 13 feet), which is very important. This morning, it was learned from the bureau that the high tide last night did not reach the predicted level, but was only 11 feet 1 inch, 1 foot 1 inch lower than predicted. Therefore, during the high tide time, except for the rapid currents, the roads and embankments were not affected.

Next Month's Forecast

According to measurements, the quantity of today's and tomorrow's high tides is lower than the tide on the 18th. Therefore, if there are no strong winds and rainstorms, the high tides this month can be passed safely. As for the high tides next month, the bureau has also completed the measurements. The tides on the seven consecutive days from the 12th to the 19th will be the highest, with quantities all above 11 feet and 12 feet. In particular, the night tides on the 16th (predicted 12 feet 5 and a half inches), the 17th (predicted 12 feet 6 and a half inches), and the 18th (12 feet 6 inches) will be very high.

Urge Removal of Stored Goods

In addition, the Dada Shipping Company and the Datong Shipping Company announced, "To whom it may concern: The autumn flood is approaching and is difficult to predict. For goods stored by cargo owners in the company's own or leased warehouses, those stacked on the ground floor must be taken away or moved to another warehouse during the flood season. Otherwise, if there is any damage, it is an act of God and difficult for people to resist. The companies will not be responsible. However, within the possible range, we will do our best to protect them. The losses and expenses incurred due to the protection will still be borne by the cargo owners. This is a special announcement, for your information."

Banks and Brokers Agree on a Flexible Arrangement for Foreign Exchange Commissions; 1/32 for Banks and Banks; 1/16 for Banks and Customer Accounts 108

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, after the Shanghai Foreign Exchange Banks Association decided to reduce the foreign exchange commission for brokers from 1/16 to 1/32 starting on September 1, the Japanese brokers were the first to oppose it and requested the Foreign Exchange Brokers Association to file a complaint. The Brokers Association held a meeting in Shanghai and resolved to request a remedy. Now, after negotiation between the chairman of the Brokers Association and the chairman of the Foreign Exchange Banks Association, a flexible arrangement has been decided: (1) For foreign exchange transactions between banks, the broker's commission will be reduced to 1/32; (2) For foreign exchange transactions between banks and customer accounts, the broker's commission will remain at the current level of 1/16. The above arrangement will become official after it is approved by the Foreign Exchange Brokers Association and the Brokers Association sends a letter to the Foreign Exchange Banks Association.

Yang Jianzhong, an Important Witness in the Japanese Sailor Case, Was Interrogated Yesterday; Yang Firmly Denies Planting Evidence and Framing; Face-to-Face Confrontation with Yang Wendao in Court 109

Yang Wendao from Guangdong was arrested by the police in the First Special District Court along with Ye Haisheng, Zhou Sherong, and others for being involved in the murder of Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo. The court has repeatedly opened hearings to investigate the case. Because Yang initially admitted that the handgun and book found in his home belonged to him, but then suddenly claimed that his relative Yang Jianzhong planted the evidence and framed him, Yang Jianzhong became an important witness in the case. The court specially ordered the police to investigate and summon him for questioning. Since Jianzhong had already left Shanghai, it was difficult to obtain substantial evidence as to whether Wendao's accusation of planting the evidence was true. Until the other day, Yang Jianzhong turned himself in to the police, declaring that he was willing to go to court for questioning. Therefore, Judge Xiao Xiefen of the First Special District Court reopened the investigation hearing at 2 p.m. yesterday. Prosecutor Tang also attended the hearing to perform his duties. The Japanese side also sent military personnel to the court to listen. Yang Wendao's defense lawyers, Tang Huaiqun and Guo Qiming, also appeared in court one after another. Because only the book was being investigated, only Yang Wendao was escorted to court by the police.

The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that the defendant Yang Wendao admitted during the first and second preliminary hearings that the book with a hole dug in it to hide the handgun used to kill Nakayama Hideo, which was seized from his home, belonged to him, and that the hole in the book was indeed for hiding the gun. The police confirmed that the gun hidden in the hole was the gun used to kill the Japanese sailor. Yang only changed his previous confession during the third interrogation, claiming that the book found was planted by Yang Jianzhong in his home to frame him. However, he has not been able to prove this statement. Fortunately, Yang Jianzhong turned himself in to the police yesterday, claiming that although he and Wendao shared the same surname, they were not of the same clan. He did not know about Wendao's matters and could not have gone to his house to plant evidence and frame him. Since Wendao's arrest, he has been repeatedly threatened. To avoid danger, he left Shanghai. However, thinking that this matter could not be resolved by avoiding it for long, he resolutely turned himself in to clarify the truth. Yang Jianzhong has been brought to court, and the court is requested to investigate. The court then interrogated Yang Jianzhong, who stated that he was 53 years old, currently residing at No. 377, Hong An Lane, Lao Ba Zi Road. He and Yang Wendao were from the same family 700 years ago. Because they both belong to the Beishan Yang clan, they are members of the Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association, so they know each other. I call him uncle. Since meeting him at the Tongren Association operated by Wendao in August of last year, I have not seen him again. If I had ever been to his home, his family would certainly recognize me, and I could call them to identify me.

The court then showed Jianzhong the book with the hole for hiding the gun that was seized from Wendao's home. After viewing it, Jianzhong replied that he had never seen this book before, and never taught Wendao how to dig a hole in the book to hide a gun. He also said that I have tens of thousands of dollars in property, why would I need to borrow from Wendao. When questioned about Yang Wendao's statement, he said that in October of the 22nd year, I visited Wendao at the Taikoo warehouse. I happened to have a handgun that I had nowhere to store properly, and Jianzhong taught me how to hide the gun, saying that digging a hole in the book and hiding it would be the most appropriate. At that time, Jianzhong was wearing a woolen cap, not like the suit he wears now. I am his uncle, how could I frame him? The court then continued to investigate Jianzhong, who stated that he knew the doctor Zheng Huimin. On April 18th, Zheng came to the Beishan Fellow Villagers Association and saw the name Yang Wendao among the members. Zheng asked me if I knew Wendao's address, saying that the police wanted to find Wendao. At the time of the conversation, another member, Yang Guimei, wrote Wendao's address on a cigarette card and gave it to Zheng. Later, Zheng came to visit me again, saying that he had gone to the address and learned that Wendao did not live there. I then led Zheng to Yang Guimei's house, where they conducted their own inquiries. When Zheng first asked me, he did not promise me any reward if I found Wendao's whereabouts, nor did he explain the reason for looking for Wendao. Later, when Wendao was arrested, I learned about it from the newspaper. Unexpectedly, the atmosphere towards me has become increasingly bad since then, so I went to Guangzhou temporarily to avoid it. After returning to Shanghai, I traveled to Beijing, Hangzhou, and other places. Now, if this matter is not clarified, it will not only damage my reputation but also make it difficult to do business, so I specially turned myself in. However, Yang Jiaodao claimed that Yang Jianzhong told Yang Guimei that the police were arresting people very tightly and asked Guimei to come and inform him to flee quickly. Yang Jianzhong denied Yang Wendao's statement. Therefore, the two Yangs were confronted face-to-face. Judge Xiao announced that the court was adjourned because the investigation into this part had produced substantial results. Yang Wendao was still taken back to the police station for detention. Yang Jianzhong was taken to the police station's fingerprint office to have his fingerprints taken for verification according to law.

Last Night's Thunderstorm in the City - Heavy Thunderstorm Around the Fish Market Area - No Rain in the French Concession and Other Places 110

The weather in this port city, after the start of autumn, though briefly cooler, suddenly became unusually hot again from the day before, resembling the heat of midsummer. Rampant Water Bandits in the Jiangyin Area - Merchants Request Strict Apprehension - All Dressed in Gray Uniforms, Robbing 111

In the Yangtze River area along Jiangyin and Zhenjiang, water bandits frequently appear, and merchant ships traveling to and fro are often robbed. Previously, Yan Yongxiao, the director of the Shanghai Joint Office of the Zhejiang Eastern Saltpeter Boat Industry, submitted a report to the Fourth District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, requesting strict investigation and apprehension. Subsequently, an instruction was received stating that the area was no longer under the jurisdiction of the Fourth District and that a separate request should be submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs. Xiao then prepared a document yesterday and submitted it to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, requesting the dispatch of police for investigation and suppression. The original text stated: "Submitting a report for the rampant activities of bandits and repeated robbery cases, requesting strict suppression to ensure the safety of merchants." This office has repeatedly received reports from its affiliated Jin Shun Cai Boat, Wu Tai Xing Boat, Xin Kai Tai Boat, Xin Heng Yuan Boat, Shen Zheng Xing Boat, Wang Shun Xing Boat, Wu Tong Xing Boat, Xin Fu Li Boat, Ma Wan Xing Boat, Xin Tong Xing Boat, Song Yi Xing Boat, Qian Shun Xing Boat, etc., stating that the boats transport goods from Shanghai to Nanchang, Zhenjiang, and other places. Along the way, in the area of about 200 kilometers between Jiangyin and Zhenjiang, they often encounter bandits at midnight. These bandits are usually seven or eight people, wearing gray uniforms and holding modern firearms. They jump from small sand boats onto the boats, claiming to inspect for contraband but in reality robbing. Afterwards, they leave triumphantly. Among them, the Qian Shun Xing Boat was robbed on the 30th of last month, and the boatman Shi Jinren was shot and seriously wounded, with a bullet through his palm. He is currently being treated in a Shanghai hospital. Based on this, this office prepared a document and submitted it to the Fourth District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, requesting intensified patrols and apprehension to bring the criminals to justice. Subsequently, on the 11th of this month, a reply was received stating: "The report is noted. Since the reorganization last year, the Yangtze River area is no longer under the jurisdiction of this district. The request to dispatch patrol boats and intensify patrols is difficult to comply with. You should submit the request directly to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs." In view of this, it is found that the area around Jiangyin and Zhenjiang is supposed to be peaceful and stable. However, since December of last year, robbery cases have occurred repeatedly. Moreover, these bandits are wearing gray uniforms and carrying firearms, daring to be blatant and rampant. Whether they are bandits or not is unknown. Judging from their actions and clothing, it is highly suspicious. Therefore, this document is submitted again, requesting your review and approval, and to order the dispatch of capable police officers to intensify patrols in the area before and after Jiangyin and Zhenjiang, especially during midnight hours, in order to curb banditry and ensure the safety of merchants. This would be a great act of kindness. Respectfully submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, by Yan Yongxiao, Director of the Shanghai Joint Office of the Zhejiang Eastern Saltpeter Boat Industry."

Buddhist Association's Baojing Accepts Leadership of Mogan Mountain Lotus Society 112

Datong News Agency reports that prominent figures from the government and society, such as Zhang Jingjiang, Dai Jitao, Huang Yingbai, Zhang Xiaolin, Shi Shengzhi, and others, in order to eliminate the disasters of the times, initiated the construction of a Lotus Society on Mogan Mountain. Construction began a year ago and has now been completed. A letter was specially sent to invite Master Baojing, the director of the Shanghai Chinese Buddhist Association, to be the president. The monk has already agreed. The correspondence between them is transcribed below:

Letter of Invitation 113

Reverend Master Baojing, I respectfully write to inform you that last year, we and others, recognizing that the disasters of the times are frequent and that only by promoting Buddhism can they be eliminated, initiated the organization of a Lotus Society on Mogan Mountain, with the goal of benefiting both oneself and others. After a year, it has fortunately been completed. However, considering that the position of president is of utmost importance at the beginning of the establishment, only those with grand aspirations and a resounding reputation can shoulder this important task. After deliberation, we have unanimously decided to invite you to take on the position of president and entrust you with full authority. It is clear that you are a renowned contemporary figure and are widely respected. We cannot help but admire you. We respectfully prepare this letter of invitation and sincerely hope that you will compassionately accept it and benefit all sentient beings. Share the remaining glow of Mount Tiantai to illuminate this land, and the old site of Jinzhong is destined to have a previous connection. Continue the unfinished wish of the late Master, and the joy of the Western Paradise is imaginable. By promoting the teachings of Master Si Ming Zun Zhe, the light of the Tiantai School will be boundless. The future of the Buddhist Association relies heavily on this, and the remedy for people's hearts depends on your guidance. We eagerly await your auspicious cloud and offer our heartfelt prayers. Respectfully wishing you peace. Zhang Renjie, Dai Chuanxian, Shi Zhizhao, Zhang Xiaolin, Huang Yingbai, and others, the initiators and founders of the Mogan Mountain Lotus Society.

Reply Letter

Jingjiang, Shengzhi, Xiaolin, Yingbai, and all great lay Buddhists, I have received your letter and respectfully acknowledge its kind intentions. I am unworthy and unqualified to be entrusted with the position of president of the Mogan Mountain Lotus Society. I respectfully admire your noble aspirations and great compassion. On the beautiful Mogan Mountain, you are continuing the legacy of Mount Lu, cultivating mindfulness of the Buddha, and upholding the Dharma in the degenerate age. You are riding the great vow boat to reverse the disasters of the coming age. Your merits are immeasurable, and everyone rejoices. Although I have inherited the robe and bowl, I have not received the transmission of the lamp. I lack eloquence and have no reputation. However, I am determined to help sentient beings and am compassionate. Moreover, I am repeatedly urged to take on this task. Therefore, I should lead monastics and lay followers to diligently practice Pure Land Buddhism and encourage the awakening of Bodhicitta. I hope that there will be a mutual response and that virtuous roots will be widely planted. May the sound of the bell be carried by the wind, and may the villagers commonly understand the teachings. May the bamboo path be filled with clouds, and may the great Bodhisattva's image be seen in this land. With utmost sincerity, I dedicate this merit to all of you. I respectfully reply to this letter and wish you pure joy. Huai Jing He Nan.

Shen Xingmin and Chen Qu from Ningbo colluded with the fugitive mastermind Wang Jinbao. Between the 29th of last month and the 12th of this month, they rented a side room at No. 540 Dong Youheng Road, hanging two signs outside: "Tian Er Film Company Preparatory Office" and "Affiliated Tian Er Dance Research Society." They advertised in newspapers to recruit dozens of actors, tea servants, etc. to practice filming, and defrauded them of guarantee deposits, meal expenses, and registration fees. Zhao Qingxun from Hangzhou, who was fooled into becoming a tea servant, was defrauded of a 20-yuan guarantee deposit. Jiao Ziping from Shandong, who was learning photography, was defrauded of 7 yuan for meals. After the case was exposed by Zhao and Jiao, the group attempted to flee to Xi'an. The case was reported to the Maoshan Police Station detective Zhao Yongqing, and with the assistance of Chinese constables No. 1967 and No. 1876, Shen Xingmin was arrested first, and Chen Qu was apprehended at room No. 25 of the North Station Grand Hotel. This has already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhong Qing presided over the hearing in the Second Criminal Court. Municipal Council lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that two letters requesting the company's regulations, sent from other places and affixed with postage stamps, had been used up. A military certificate claiming that Chen Qu was a staff member of the First Section of the Club of the Military Commission in Xi'an was found in Chen Qu's room at the North Station Grand Hotel, but its authenticity is unknown. Also, three iron irons and more than thirty wooden clothes dyes that Shen Xingmin planned to use with Chen to open a laundry in Xi'an, a washboard, and three straw hat stretchers were found. Xia Hengmei, Liu Zhengxiang, Zhu Ji, and three others who intended to serve as tea servants in the company were defrauded of a total of 8 yuan in registration fees. He requested that they be severely punished. All the evidence was presented for inspection. Next, the two witnesses, Xia and Liu, testified about the process of being defrauded of registration fees. The two defendants were questioned, and their statements were evasive and pleading for leniency. Judge Zhong ruled that they should be remanded in custody, and the sentence would be pronounced on a scheduled date.
