"Don't Cry" Turns Out to be a Prophecy - Wang Huizhong Drowns - Farewell to His Wife Before Departure - Swept Away by a Big Wave and Drowned Instantly 119

Wang Huizhong, a local resident, 27 years old, lived at No. 79 Taopeng Road, Yangshupu. He had been working at the Municipal Council Donations Office collecting wharf donations for a year and a half. He had his father, Wang Yongkui, and mother at home, and he had just married his wife two months ago. Wang Huizhong had requested to be transferred to another position because of the danger of traveling back and forth on the river, and the request was being reviewed. At 8:00 AM the previous morning, Wang Huizhong went out to work and suddenly said goodbye to his wife, "I'm going out now, don't cry." The family thought it was a joke and didn't take it seriously. Unexpectedly, it turned out to be a prophecy. At about 10:10 AM, Wang Huizhong and his Indian assistant went to the Huishan Wharf and were recording the ship numbers when a large wave swept over. Wang was standing by the ship, and the wave knocked him off his feet and drowned him. The water police immediately fished him out, but he was already dead. The detective Yao Guofa took the body to the South Wharf Lifesaving Bureau and reported it to the local court. Prosecutor Zhu and inspectors Shen, etc. arrived at the scene to examine the body and ordered the family to collect it for burial.

Some of the stolen items were hidden in the home of Wang Jiangong at No. 160, Yongfengfang, North Sichuan Road. The police arrested Wang and searched out some of the stolen goods. Wheat Exports - Request for Prohibition - First Special District Joint Association Submits to the Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Industry 122

The First Special District Citizens' Joint Association, in order to request the swift issuance of a ban to prohibit wheat exports in order to maintain the national economy and the people's livelihood, specially submitted reports to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry yesterday. The original report stated: "Submitting a report to request the prohibition of wheat exports in order to maintain the national economy and the people's livelihood. Our country is an agricultural country. Due to frequent floods and droughts, production is insufficient, resulting in the intrusion of foreign rice and wheat into the market, forming a huge drain on the national economy. This year, due to the great climatic harmony, the wheat-producing areas of Hebei, Shanxi, Shaanxi, and Shandong provinces have all reported bumper harvests. However, Japanese merchants take advantage of our low wheat prices and purchase it in large quantities, and unscrupulous Chinese merchants are helping to fuel the situation. It is heard that those transporting for export have already reached 300,000 dan, and Japanese merchants are still continuing to purchase. This matter has a profound impact on the future of the people's food supply and the flour industry. We believe that in order to reasonably solve the wheat export problem, we should internally examine the domestic food needs and externally observe the world wheat market, so that we will not incur debts. This association believes that wheat should be prohibited from export today. The reasons are as follows: According to wheat as a raw material for flour milling, the raw materials of flour mills in Shanghai, Wuxi, and other places have always relied on the wheat production in the Yangtze River basin, which can only be used by flour mills for seven or eight months. Although the wheat production in Hebei, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Shandong, and other provinces has a bumper harvest this year, the Yangtze River basin is still average. If we immediately recognize that there is an excess and allow it to be exported at a low price, then the raw materials of the flour mills will be exhausted in an instant, and we will have to repurchase high-priced foreign wheat for relief. Between one export and one import, the loss is very large. Moreover, the flour mills can expect to be prosperous in foreign sales due to the low cost of domestic wheat. This is from the perspective of the flour mills established by the Chinese people, and the export should be prohibited. Those who advocate wheat exports argue that the cheap grain hurts farmers, believing that excess domestic wheat will inevitably lead to a sharp drop in wheat prices, which will affect the economy. However, they do not know that there has been frequent famine in the country for years, and the people lack food reserves. Not only is there no fear of excess, but it is still difficult to be self-sufficient. At the same time, Chinese flour mills are relying on domestic wheat for supply, and the supply and demand are appropriate. There is no concern that wheat prices will be too low. Today, if we sell wheat at five yuan per dan, and then buy foreign wheat at more than five yuan, is it not enough to worry about the impact of expensive grain on the people's food? This is from the perspective of the people's food supply, and the export should be prohibited. At a time when the international situation is becoming increasingly urgent, national defense food is extremely important. If we do not control it and allow people to buy it, then once something happens, the country will lack food, and how can we maintain the morale of the army and the people? Therefore, even if there is an excess of domestic wheat, it should not be exported. This is from the perspective of national defense food, and the export should be prohibited. In summary, all of the above shows that wheat exports have many crises. Therefore, we especially request your ministry to quickly issue a ban to prohibit wheat exports in order to maintain the national economy and the people's livelihood. We are anxiously looking forward to it. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry."

Wu Liang, a 45-year-old woman from Anhui, was working as a maid at No. 24, Jianye Lane, Fuli Road, French Concession. Wang Shen, a 34-year-old woman from the same village, was also working as a maid at No. 25 in the same lane. The two women lived next door. Aftermath of the Drum Singer's Suicide Case: Wang Chenglu Accused, Drum Singer's Parents Sue for Damages 125

Zhang Yueqin, a female drum singer from Hebei, was invited to Shanghai last winter to perform at the Central Hotel on Fuzhou Road. She became involved with Wang Chenglu, a salt merchant from Anhui residing in Shanghai. Wang intended to take her as a concubine, but they could not agree on terms. As a result, the woman committed suicide by taking poison on June 19th at the Xindu Apartment in Daode Lane, Beile Road in the French Concession. The Special No. 2 Court dispatched personnel to investigate and verify the circumstances. Later, Wang provided funds for the woman's father, Zhang Haishan, to arrange for the coffin and burial. This was previously reported. However, after Yueqin's death, Wang promised to settle the living arrangements for the woman's parents, so Zhang Haishan, the father, exonerated Wang at the verification site. Contrary to expectations, after the body was coffined and buried, Wang broke his promise and disregarded the living needs of Zhang Haishan and his wife, Madam Zhang Zhao. Zhang Haishan believes that his daughter was seduced and killed by Wang and that he himself was tricked. Unwilling to accept this, he recently hired a lawyer to file a complaint in the Criminal Court of the Special No. 1 Court, accusing Wang Chenglu of causing death with the intent of adultery, according to Articles 298, Section 2 and 302, Section 2 of the Criminal Law. The complaint states that the defendant Wang Chenglu, a native of Anhui, with the alias "Master Taotan," is 34 years old this year and resides at No. 14 Jingyu Lane, Weihaiwei Road. He is currently the General Manager of the Dayuan Salt Factory. Last winter, the plaintiff's daughter, Yueqin, was invited to Shanghai to perform at the Central Hotel for a monthly salary of one hundred yuan. After the two-month term, she was hired to perform at the Xiao Guang Han theater. At that time, Wang Chenglu came to listen to the performances and, seeing Yueqin's beauty, harbored intentions of seduction. Initially, he used ordering songs to display his wealth, and then he frequently gave gifts to show his attentiveness, causing the vulnerable woman to fall into his trap. He then had relations with her at No. 10 and No. 31 Xindu Apartment, No. 1 Daode Lane, Beile Road in the French Concession. From then on, the two secretly engaged in intimacy, sharing meals and lodging. Just as the two were passionately in love, Wang Haiting, the manager of the Nanjing Confucius Temple branch of the "Yet World", planned to send her to perform in Beijing. Yueqin went to Beijing in April of this year. In less than a month, Wang Chenglu sent Sang and Yang to Beijing to bring her back. Because the contract was not yet complete, Sang and Yang secretly plotted to bring her back to Shanghai. However, when they arrived at Nanjing Station, "Yet World" found out and sent people to bring Yueqin back. Sang and Yang brought the luggage and clothes to Shanghai and stored them at home. Yueqin was unable to perform in Beijing, so she also came to Shanghai. Wang Chenglu offered to pay one thousand yuan to take Yueqin as a concubine. The plaintiff couple, having only one daughter, were unwilling to sell her as a concubine for a thousand yuan and firmly refused. However, Yueqin's will was weak and she was seduced by Wang's money and power. On June 19th of this year, feeling that good things would not come to fruition, she committed suicide by ingesting opium. The defendant sent her to the Niu Min Sanatorium on Weihaiwei Road for treatment. Because the poisoning was severe, she died on June 20th. The defendant arranged for the coffin and burial at No. 4930 Jiangning Public Cemetery on Xinza Road. On July 22nd, the defendant sent Sang and Yang to return Yueqin's luggage. It was discovered that many items of clothing were missing. The death of their daughter was entirely caused by the defendant. They requested that the defendant be punished according to the law and requested incidental civil proceedings, demanding compensation of 24,000 yuan (calculated based on Yueqin's monthly salary of 200 yuan for ten years). The court, upon receiving the complaint, summoned the plaintiff Zhang Haishan and his lawyer to the Criminal Court No. 2 yesterday morning, presided over by Judge Chen Shuoying. The defendant did not appear. The court questioned the plaintiff and ruled that he was not a direct victim and could not sue according to the law. Therefore, the case was dismissed.

Members Yikang Yuanji requested to withdraw from the association and a resolution was requested. It was resolved that all members should join the association in accordance with the law, and the request should not be discussed. Hot Water Bottle Manufacturing Industry: The Hot Water Bottle Manufacturing Trade Association had previously severely and repeatedly addressed the issue of industry sales prices, and had filed with the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for record. However, with the passage of time, these matters became neglected and many in the industry regarded them as mere formalities. Consequently, the market prices had recently become increasingly chaotic. The association, believing that continuing along this course would not benefit the industry, convened all member representatives yesterday at the start of the autumn season to conduct a thorough discussion. More than ten people attended, including Lixing Gan Dounan, Zhongguo Zhang Qingfa, Yutai Xu Shanji, Zhonghua Wu Rongxing, Xin Zhonghua Chen Fei, Zhenye Zhao Quankui, Dahu Tang Heqing, etc. After Chairman Gan Dounan opened the meeting with due ceremony, Chairman Gan Dounan reported the purpose of the meeting, and then Zhang Qingfa and Xu Shanji delivered speeches regarding the guiding principles for rectifying the sales prices. Following a thorough discussion, it was resolved that appropriate prices would be set for ordinary goods and that personnel would be dispatched immediately to various factories to affix their seals. This would then be submitted to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for record and implementation. It was also reported that the association's current efforts to rectify market prices would be strict and thorough. Anyone who attempts to undermine these prices would be severely punished to deter others.

Ice Machine Industry: The Shanghai Machine Ice Sales Trade Association, following instructions from the Municipal Party Department, appointed Wu Weiqing and eight others as members of the association's reorganization committee. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, the association held a swearing-in ceremony for the committee members at No. 2 Cheng Ye Li, Miller Road. The reorganization committee members Xu Zhantai, Wu Weiqing, Pan Zhiliang, Shen Shishan, Cheng Xiqian, Wang Xincong, Gao Abing, Gu Shaoqing, and Tang Abing, along with Wang Yucheng, representative of the City Party Department, Zhang Dafu, representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, and master of ceremonies Jin Heqin, were present. Under the leadership of representatives from the Party and government organizations, they formally swore in and discussed important proposals. The meeting adjourned after the ceremony.

New Medicine Industry: The New Medicine Trade Association, after the members' representative assembly, nominated Xu Xiangsun, Gao Peiliang, Pan Ruitang, Shi Zhifu and 19 others, for the Smuggling Inspection Committee, convened an inaugural meeting the day before yesterday. Xu Xiaochu was publicly elected as chairman, dividing into general affairs, inspection, identification and communication groups, which Xu Chao, Yuan Hesong, Tu Kaizheng, Zhou Bangjun served concurrently as standing committee members, Sun Choucheng served concurrently as Director Secretary. Twelve inspection regulations were formulated, and forms such as volunteer applications and registration forms were stipulated, which were sent to members for compliance.

The attending members were Zhang Xuejian, Sun Jian, Zhang Guochang, Lu Zuyun, Zhou Jingxuan, Tan Mingren, Wu Wanxi, Xia Huangzhong, Xu Nanyong, etc. Zhang Xuejian was publicly elected as the temporary chairman, and Liu Xiaotian recorded the minutes. It will also join the City Chamber of Commerce. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Meat Sold in Vegetable Markets Must Be Deboned; Butchers Oppose; Cattle and Sheep Trade Association Asks Chamber of Commerce to Negotiate for Cancellation 128

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the butchers in the Hongkou vegetable market of this city received a notice from the Public Works Department's Health Department yesterday, prohibiting the deboning of meat in the vegetable market from today. All the butchers are strongly opposed to this, and the situation is very urgent. The letter from the butchers requesting the Cattle and Sheep Trade Association to ask the City Chamber of Commerce to negotiate for cancellation is excerpted as follows: A humble submission from member associations: It is reported that the Municipal Council Health Department has instructed our butchers to transport the butchered meat to the fresh meat market established by the department for deboning and wholesale and retail. In addition, each cow must increase the cost by one yuan and three dimes five cents, which is a total of two yuan and three dimes five cents with the slaughter fee of one yuan. This method is cumbersome, the burden is too heavy, and it hinders business. We have already described the difficulties and requested your association to negotiate for cancellation. As a result, an agreement was reached with the Health Department that our butchers would pay the fee, with each cow paying a total of one yuan and five dimes with the slaughter fee, and beef, mutton and pork would each increase by five dimes. The original livestock maintenance fees and hot and cold water fees stipulated by the slaughterhouse are now included in the one yuan and five dimes. The cold storage in the fresh meat market is allowed to store fresh meat for free within a week, and is allowed to be exempt from entering the market for work. The burden of the fees is already unbearable. However, in order to avoid the various difficulties of the fresh meat market, members are willing to pay the fee of one yuan and five dimes per cow, which is already a strain. Unexpectedly, only a few months later, the Municipal Council Health Department changed the previous agreement and issued a notice on the 5th of this month, stating that from today onwards, the deboning, trimming and packaging of meat are strictly prohibited in the Hongkou vegetable market and must be carried out in the Municipal Council's meat market specifically for this purpose. This is hereby announced. Reading this, we are deeply horrified. If this system is implemented, members will have to spend a lot of procedures and time, and will suffer from the pain of hindering business, which is really unbearable. Therefore, the difficulties are once again presented to your association. The members slaughter cattle and sheep in the Municipal Council's slaughterhouse, and the slaughterhouse transports them to the vegetable market for deboning and retail sales. The work has been going on at the same time without any differences. However, the Municipal Council has set up this new system. Now, the members must first transport the daily slaughtered meat to the fresh meat market established by the bureau for deboning, and then transport the deboned meat to the vegetable market for sale. This method is extremely difficult and is definitely an impossible fact. Usually, meat is sold every morning at two or three o'clock. The meat must be transported to the vegetable market, deboned and sold to facilitate business. If it is first transported to the fresh meat market for deboning, it will be past the time of purchase and sale, and the meat will be discolored due to multiple handling and frequent movement, and it will easily breed mold. If it is said to be hygienic, it will be counterproductive. According to the hygiene of citizens' meat consumption, there will be obstacles. Moreover, meat buyers often buy meat that has not been deboned (catering companies, Chinese and Western restaurants, and Chinese and Western people often buy it) for cooking. If the bones are removed before the sale, buyers will inevitably sigh at the disappearance of the market. The quantity and quality of the goods sold by members will inevitably shrink. Both supply and demand will be affected. In addition, multiple transfers, frequent transportation, and increased losses are even more unbearable. In addition, the slaughterhouse in the French Concession transports the meat to the Hongkou vegetable market for sale. The bones and meat must be connected before they can be split to the industry. If deboning is not allowed in the vegetable market, it is tantamount to prohibiting the transportation and sale of the meat. The business of our industry will inevitably be reduced. This is also a difficult end. Moreover, members in the same industry often have the fact that there is a surplus in this place and a shortage in that place, or a surplus in that place and a shortage in this place. They split each other to make up for the shortage every day. If the bones have been removed in advance, there is no way to adjust the surplus and the shortage. Those who are short will inevitably reduce their business, and those who are surplus will have no way to sell them. Both parties will suffer. Because members in the same industry must have bones and meat connected to each other in order to meet the market, this is also a difficult task to remove the bones before the sale. The reason for the members' opposition lies in this. If this system is implemented, the direct and indirect losses of the members will be indescribable. As for the members, they rent shops and stalls from the Municipal Council and have signed all the regulations to abide by. It is not much different from renting houses and doing business in other cities. Check the landlords and shops, rent them to others, and have stipulated certain procedures when signing the lease. If the shop is handled after the rental, it is the business of the lessee, but there has never been a case where the tenant is rented and then arbitrarily increases the harsh rules and arbitrarily interferes. When the members rented the stalls, the vegetable market regulations did not have such harsh rules. Now, they arbitrarily change the rules, which is no different from the landlord and the shop renting out the shop and then arbitrarily interfering and hindering the tenant's business. Members feel all kinds of difficulties, and it is really difficult to comply with this system. If the authorities do not understand and force the implementation, the members can only accept the sacrifice of closure and swear not to accept the new system that wastes time, hinders business, wastes transportation costs, and hinders hygiene. If the Municipal Council builds this building as a fresh meat market and the butchers do not use it, it is a pity, it can be used for other purposes. Why must it be unchanged and forcibly used for the needs of the meat market? Things are precious because they are applicable. If they are not applicable and forcibly used, is it not equal to the disadvantage of cutting the feet to fit the shoes? It is not only useless, but also harmful. Now, the fresh meat market is not suitable for the needs of our butchers. If we force it to be used, the harm will be very serious. Therefore, we humbly submit that we beg your association to quickly appeal to the Municipal Council to revoke it, and also ask the City Chamber of Commerce to send a letter to negotiate and must achieve the purpose of cancellation before it is over. So, the industry association finds that the Municipal Council's efforts to build a fresh meat market and to have the butchers transport meat into the market to organize various tasks such as dividing meat and removing bones are well-intentioned, but because the fresh meat market is too far away from the small vegetable market, there are many obstacles. The extension of the ancestral period, the obstruction of business, the increase of unnecessary transportation costs, and the damage to the original quality of meat are all hindering the butchers. The business is really suffering a great loss. The members of the association have repeatedly called for revocation, and it is also appropriate. In order to maintain the business of its members, the association, based on the previous situation, has appealed on behalf of the members. In addition to sending a letter to the Municipal Council to apply for revocation, it also asks the Municipal Council to understand the business situation and revoke it immediately. It is a public concern. I humbly submit it to Wang, Chairman of the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce.

Bishop Yu Bin's Ordination Scheduled for September 20th in Beiping 129

Since Dr. Yu Bin, General Supervisor of the National Catholic Action, received a telegram from the Roman Curia on August 8th, officially appointing him as Bishop of the Nanjing Diocese, Catholic believers and organizations across the country, as well as his friends and ministers and committee members of the National Government, have sent telegrams of congratulations and warm welcomes. In addition to Catholics, other classmates, fellow villagers, and friends working in Beijing are enthusiastically participating. It is now learned that Bishop Yu has received a telegram from Rome stating that the papal appointment decree has been issued and will arrive before mid-September. Electric Wire Breaks, Touching Old Ba's Right Arm 130

At 7:20 last night, the electric wire along Fangbang Road in the city in front of the Town God's Temple suddenly broke and fell. It happened that Lao Ba (40 years old, from Nanjing), a fruit vendor on the roadside, was touched on his right arm by the broken electric wire and immediately fainted. Fortunately, a clerk from Dachang Candle Shop saw it and used a bamboo pole to pick it away, avoiding being burned to death, but he was seriously injured. The police officer on duty sent him to Shanghai Hospital for treatment and reported the incident to the police station for investigation.

Fire at Mingde Girls' School Destroys Eleven Rooms 131

The large residence of the Liu family at No. 2 Huajin Lane, Huajin Road, Sanpailou in the city, which is now being rented to Mingde Girls' Vocational High School as a school building, suddenly caught fire in the kitchen due to careless cooking at 4:40 yesterday afternoon. The fire quickly became uncontrollable. The fire engines arrived and made every effort to extinguish the fire, which was finally extinguished at 5:30. Eleven rooms, including the chemistry lab, typing classroom, internship bank room, auditorium, and dormitory, were destroyed, resulting in significant losses. Afterwards, the Shanzhong Police Station took Cai Linsheng, the school's janitor, to the Town God's Temple Police Station for questioning. It is reported that only 2,000 yuan of fire insurance was held.

A Record of the Lishi Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition 135

The large-scale calligraphy and painting exhibition of the Lishi Society has been published in the newspapers for several days. I was eager to go to see it, but I was too busy with trivial matters. Only yesterday did I take the time to go and see it. Sure enough, it was full of colorful lights and sparkling sights. It can be said that it is a grand gathering of the works of dozens of famous artists in Shanghai. Among them, the excellent works are too numerous to appreciate fully. For example, Zhang Dazhuang's old brush is scattered, Qian Huafu's Buddha paintings are full of ancient meaning, Yuan Songnian's spirit and form are both present, Zhang Shuqi's carefully crafted works, and Hu Zaobin's rich and meticulous works are all worthy of savoring and unforgettable. In calligraphy, Zhang Xiaolou's Zhang Paper Calligraphy Manual is powerful and spirited. It is not necessary to imitate Wu Jun to have a place of one's own. Fen Weng's large-scale tablet style, at first glance, seems to be imitating He Xiang, but in fact, the spirit and reason are transcended, and it is superior to the realm of the Han people. Li Que's calligraphy has many types and is excellent in all styles. His Wei stele streamers are indeed his family style, with a distant realm of the right beginning, similar to precise inspection. His big seal script, like the Lin Qian, is truly a spiritual journey of the three dynasties and never lingers in the two Lis. Regardless of Deng and Wang's suddenness, if he makes Qin seal script, such as Lin Qin Liangwen, then he must be the pen of the heroic and dangerous . His walking revolution imitates Lu Gong's large-scale work, which is especially a masterpiece. There is a great Mihai palace comment on the book Bin, the so-called dragons and snakes flying, and the eyes of the viewers are surprised. There are also small screens made by the Four Masters of the Song Dynasty, with the faces of each family lifelike. There is also a person in this book who can truly get the spirit of Su Shi. Tian Jizai's Lin Sanpan is also ancient, powerful, and very different from those who use small seal script to write Zhong Dingwen. There are many other joint works by various artists, which cannot be listed. I not only enjoyed the visual feast, but also opened my eyes. I happily recorded it. (Meng Jiao)

Mr. Ruan Bokang's Calligraphy Style 136

Ruan Kai, styled Bokang, a calligrapher from Zhejiang, also known as Master Sizhai, based his calligraphy on the styles of Zhong Yao and Wang Xizhi, and drew from Gu Kaizhi and Liu Gongquan. He was skilled in all forms of writing, including Dian script, seal script, official script, and inscriptions on oracle bones and bronze vessels. He also excelled in seal carving, favoring plum blossom and bamboo motifs. He was highly regarded in artistic circles. He is now accepting commissions at the Xin Xue Hui She Bookstore on Jiaotong Road in this city. His rates are not high. It is known that members of society who wish to connect with him through the art of calligraphy will find a flourishing opportunity here, akin to a scenic route.

Disputes Over the Property of Xiangxuetang, Custodian Wei Xia Declares 137

According to Xinsheng News Agency, the fresh meat industry in this city has traditionally been divided into Shanghai, Ningbo, and Jiangsu factions. The Xiangyuntang Public Hall and all its assets are the common property of the Shanghai meat industry in the southern part of the city. The land certificate of the public hall was originally held by Yan Weixiao, and for more than ten years, things were peaceful. Unexpectedly, recently, Zhu Zhigao, Liu Zengxiang, and others intended to take out the land certificate to mortgage a large sum of money to build new slaughterhouses in the southern part of the city. However, Yan Weixiao, due to his custodial responsibility, insisted on refusing without the consent of the entire Shanghai meat industry. The two sides held opposing views, leading to each side publishing their arguments in the newspapers, causing unrest among the fellow meat traders. Who is right and who is wrong will eventually be judged fairly. The original letter of reply from Yan Weixiao to all members of the Xiangxuetang Public Hall is transcribed as follows:

"Regarding the matter of the Xiangxuetang property, I previously published a statement in the newspaper Shen Tong Sheng. Now, having read the urgent statements in response from more than eighty firms including Xinsheng Da and others on the tenth of this month, I, Weixiao, am filled with fear and trepidation. I humbly believe that my virtue is insufficient to convince people, my talent is insufficient to manage changes, and my disposition is extremely dull. Only because of the exhortations and entrustment of the late Qian Jinfusheng and Zhao Jun Shenrong and other seniors, was I entrusted with the custody of the property. As a member of our industry, I, Weixiao, cannot shirk my duty. Unexpectedly, over the years, the debts owed by the public hall have not been cleared. In the public hall meetings, my custody of the property has never been mentioned in the general assembly. In all matters of the industry, I, Weixiao, have always adhered to the old ways as my duty, and dared not easily change course. Yet, this small matter of building a house has led to this dispute. Firms such as Xinsheng and others have exhaustively attacked me, even saying that I am stirring up trouble, reversing right and wrong, deceiving my colleagues, burying my head in the sand, ignoring the facts, spreading rumors, and arbitrarily slandering me. It would not be difficult for me to file a complaint under Article 310, but I fear that infighting among colleagues will make us a laughingstock to outsiders. How can this be good for the industry? It is not that I, Weixiao, am willing to endure insults as if blind and deaf. Now, I will address each question raised, based on the facts, one by one as follows:

(1) Regarding the collapse of the public hall's building in 1927, the officials in charge of the year and month gathered the directors and repeatedly considered the matter. They all agreed that the dilapidated state of the public hall could not be tolerated for long, as it concerned the reputation of the industry and affected appearances. However, construction with accumulated funds would not be sufficient. Therefore, Qian and others were recommended to supervise and work with me, Gangxiao, to establish the Jiyi Company, raise funds, and assist in this righteous cause. Any member of our industry with the ambition could join as a Jiyi shareholder. At that time, Xiangxue Public Hall and the Jiyi shareholders each appointed representatives to sign a formal contract, which has been followed ever since. If the leaders had not planned and the colleagues had not supported it, then for more than ten years, my colleagues would have already reported and corrected it. Why wait until today to trouble you? This is the first response.

(2) Regarding the question of whether the amount borrowed by Jiyi was stipulated in a contract, the contract specifying the amount of the loan is held by both the Public Hall and Jiyi. The original contract is naturally stored in the Public Hall. All of you are members of the Shanghai meat industry and can request to view it. Once seen, it will be clear, so there is no need for further explanation. This is the second response.

(3) Regarding the question of how Jiyi was established and whether it was registered with the Ministry of Industry, the original story of the establishment of Jiyi Company has been clearly explained in the first item. The Ministry of Industry was not yet established at that time. Moreover, Jiyi was specifically created to raise funds for the construction of the public hall, and there was no need to have representatives for external communication. The names of the representatives are listed in detail in the original contract, as mentioned above, so there is no need for further elaboration. This is the third response.

(4) Regarding the question of whether the fifteen people, including the Chief Director Qian, informed all colleagues and obtained their consent when they entrusted me, Weixiao, with the public hall's property, Chief Director Qian solicited the opinions of colleagues, and I, Weixiao, would not dare to accept the property title for safekeeping without public consent. Moreover, for more than ten years, there has not been a single dissenting opinion. What further response is needed? This is the fourth response.

(5) Regarding the question of why, after more than ten years of my custody, the public hall's annual income and expenses have never been announced, and how it still owes more than 11,000 yuan, and requesting that the annual income and expenses be announced, our public hall has always had an accountant who is specifically responsible for the huge sums of money. After the receipt of the house funds in the past, a certain amount was used each year to repay Jiyi. Both parties have records. Jiyi verified the records and there was no corruption. Since 1935, Qian and others believed that the public hall's accounts had not been cleared for a long time, and in order to quickly settle the debts and revitalize the public hall, they appointed other staff to collect rent and deliver it to Jiyi. The expenses of the public hall were paid by Mr. Zhu Zhigao. Both parties have records to prove the expenditures, which can be verified with the public hall. This is the fifth response. As for the statement that the common property of all industries in the city is currently rotated among custodians, with a maximum term of four years, I, Weixiao, have limited knowledge and experience, and I do not know the basis of this regulation. In short, Zhu Zhigao, Liu Zengxiang, and others have repeatedly expressed their intentions to me, Weixiao, recently, urging me to hand over the land certificate of Xiangxuetang for mortgaging a huge sum of 30,000 yuan to the bank. Therefore, I, Weixiao, dare not hand it over lightly. Moreover, the property management committee that they formed has not gone through legal procedures, convened meetings, or obtained the consent of the entire Shanghai meat industry. Furthermore, it has not been reported to the party and government agencies to send personnel to supervise. It is entirely manipulated by a small number of people, presenting a deceptive organization. As for the twenty-odd families out of more than eighty families who sent letters opposing my, Weixiao's, handing over the land certificate to mortgage at the bank, they are now listed in the announcement, which I, Weixiao, cannot understand. In order to clarify the truth, in addition to publishing this response in the newspaper, I also hope that you will investigate and send copies of this letter to the more than eighty firms, including Xinsheng Da. To all colleagues in the Xiangxuetang Meat Industry Public Hall."

Shanghai's Film Industry 143

— Edited by China Trust

(Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce No. 34)

4. Yi Hua Company—This company was established in September of the 22nd year of the Republic [1933], with its factory located at 1109 Connaught Road. It was a partnership organized by Yan Chuntang and others, with Yan serving as manager. The company produced sound films. Although the company's history is short, it has earned social praise for the quality of its products. The cost of each film often reaches 40,000 to 50,000 yuan. Its productions include more than ten films such as "Melee," "Woman," "Flame," "Golden Age," "Celestial Fairy," "Flying Flower Village," "Triumphal Song," "Hero of the Times," "Escape," "Rage of the China Sea," and "Incarnation Girl." The company has few basic actors, and mostly borrows them from other companies temporarily, with the salary being a certain amount paid for each film.

5. Xin Hua Company—This company was established in the 24th year of the Republic [1935] and was a partnership operated by Zhang Shanxian, owner of the Gongwu Stage, and others. Initially, there were no basic actors. The director and actors signed contracts for one or several films. The company's productions are also very careful and the content is quite good. The films that have been released include "The Story of the Red Goat Hero," "The Peach Blossom Fan," "The Song of Everlasting Sorrow," and "Peach Garden Dream," all of which are box office successes. Zhang uses the profits from the Gongwu Stage as the company's working capital, so the financial situation is quite good. It is said that Hu Ping, Tong Yuejuan, and others have now been hired as basic actors.

6. Kuai Huo Lin Company—This company was established in the 19th year of the Republic [1930] and was founded by Zhang Bingsheng, Shao Zhuanglin, and others, with Zhang as manager. The scope is quite small, with only one or two productions per year, so the company is not very noticeable to the public.

7. Shanghai Company—Established quite early, it was once merged into Lianhua. In the 23rd year [1934], it became independent again and is now engaged in the production of sound films, with a small scope.

(5) Current Status of Film Distributors

Almost all of Shanghai's film distributors are foreigners. Only two companies are operated by Chinese: Huawei Trading Company and Youlian Film Company. Among the foreign-operated companies, American companies have the greatest influence because their film industry is the most developed. The following is a breakdown:

A. Companies Established by Chinese Capital:

1. Huawei Trading Company—This company was established in March of the 18th year of the Republic [1929] with a capital of 50,000 yuan. It is located at 119 Renji Road and is a joint venture by senior staff of the Mingxing Company. Zhang Shichuan and Zhou Jianyun serve as managers, managing the productions of various companies in Shanghai, mainly those of the Mingxing Company. The annual turnover is approximately one million yuan.

2. Youlian Film Company—This company was founded by Xu Bibo. The company's address was originally located on the self-described Swei Road. Before 1932, it also produced films and had more than thirty productions. After the Shanghai Incident of 1932, the film studio was destroyed and the shareholders had no intention of continuing. Currently, the company specializes in managing its past productions, so the scope of business is quite small.

German Chancellor Hitler Awards Honorary Medals to Our Delegation Leaders; Our Country's Future Sports Trends Will Take After Germany; Will Recommend Fifteen-Year Development Plan to the Government 144

Berlin, August 18 (Kuomin Haitong News Agency) - German Interior Minister Wilhelm Frick, representing Chancellor Hitler, awarded honorary medals to Dr. Wang Zhengting, Chairman of the China National Sports Association, and Shen Siliang, Chief of the Chinese World Games delegation. Shen Siliang told the Haitong News Agency that "Modern sports in China developed relatively late, so we had no extravagant expectations for victory at the World Games from the beginning. But the greatest benefit for us was to understand the content of Germany's sports organization. China's future sports organization will also take after Germany. The Chinese Sports Association will hold a conference here to decide to recommend to the government a (fifteen-year plan) to develop Chinese sports."

When asked if the success of Chinese athletes at the World Games could be compared to the results at home, Shen said that due to weather conditions, the performance of the athletes at the World Games was worse than their results at home.

Shen also said that the organization of this World Games left a very good impression on everyone. He praised the organizational ability of the Germans and their hospitality.

When asked when the Chinese team would return home, Shen said that the football team was still playing friendly matches in Vienna and London. The rest of the team will gather in Naples on September 4 to return home.

Owens' Amateur Status to Be Lost 145

(Kuomin Haitong News Agency) Berlin, August 18 - According to Ferris, Secretary of the American Amateur Athletic Union, the amateur status of American sports star Jesse Owens, who won four gold medals at the 11th World Games, may be lost if he firmly refuses to participate in the British Stockholm Games, as he had registered to participate.

Ferris said, "Owens should go from London to Stockholm to participate in the games there, but he suddenly announced that he was considering accepting a $25,000 contract from the United States, which is enough to prove that, in principle, Owens is not opposed to becoming a professional athlete. According to the American Amateur Athletic Union's regulations, any amateur athlete who has registered to participate in a certain sport and then withdraws automatically loses their amateur status. According to this regulation, Owens may lose his amateur status because he has decided to take the Queen Mary to New York on August 19."

Black Boxer Louis Rises Again, Knocks Out Schmeling in the Third Round 146

(New York, August 18) - World heavyweight boxing star, Black boxer Joe Louis, after failing to German boxer Max Schmeling, appeared again last night (18th) at Yankee Stadium in New York, defeating former champion Jack Sharkey, starting his journey to rise again. 40,000 people watched, with the match scheduled for 15 rounds, but Sharkey was knocked out in the third round.

World Professional Boxing Championship May Not Be Held This Year 147

(Havas Agency, New York, August 18) - The World Professional Heavyweight Boxing Championship is held every year in September. The two who qualified for this year's final are German boxer Max Schmeling, who recently defeated American Black boxer Joe Louis, and American boxer James Braddock, who won the championship last year. Recently, Braddock's manager, Gould, announced that the match between Braddock and Schmeling could not be held this year because Braddock had been diagnosed by a doctor as needing surgery if he wanted to continue boxing. Therefore, Braddock will be hospitalized soon. The New York Athletic Commission is scheduled to meet tonight to decide whether to postpone the match, but regardless of the committee's decision, Gould will definitely refuse to allow Braddock to go on stage.

Accompanying the World Games Delegation: A Record 149

— (Seventh and Eighth Letters) Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen from the Central News Agency

(IV)(X) Activities of the Chinese Athletes

The Chinese athletes arrived in Berlin on the morning of the 23rd. On the afternoon of the 24th, the entire group paid their respects at the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, offering wreaths. Practice began on the 25th. Except for Jiang Bai of the soccer team, who had an eye ailment, the rest of the athletes were in good condition.

For athletes residing in the New Village, the cadre department has set a timetable: wake up at 6:30 AM (supervised by team management), raise the national flag at 7:15 AM (full uniform with trousers), breakfast from 7:30 AM to 8:15 AM, lunch from 12:00 PM to 12:45 PM, practice from 3:00 PM to 6:00 PM, lower the national flag at 6:15 PM (five participants), dinner from 6:30 PM to 7:15 PM, and bedtime at 10:30 PM. In addition, eight village rules are stipulated: (1) Be spirited, (2) Be graceful, (3) Be amiable, (4) Be neatly dressed, (5) Comply with village rules, (6) Obey instructions from Chinese staff, (7) Adhere to the schedule, and (8) Do not go out before the Games or on competition days.

Female athletes residing in the women's dormitory also observe the same rules.

Except for a dozen or so in Hamburg, members of the athletic observation group reside in camps along with observation groups from other countries. They hold meetings and listen to lectures by athletic experts from various countries every day. The work is extremely intense, and their lifestyle is just like that of soldiers, which everyone finds interesting.

Chief Delegate Wang Zhengting arrived in Berlin at 5:00 PM on the 24th with the American athletes. He visited the New Village at noon on the 25th with the Chinese Ambassador to Germany, Gan Tianfang, to express his regards to the athletes. That evening, he went to Hamburg and returned to Berlin on the 27th.

Chief Secretary Shen Siliang flew to London on the 25th to attend the Davis Cup meeting and is scheduled to return to Germany on the 28th. The martial arts team was invited to Hamburg on the 24th and gave three performances on the 25th and 26th, which were very well-received. They returned in triumph on the 27th.

The Chinese Students Association in Germany held a grand tea party at 8:00 PM on the 27th to welcome Dai Jitao, Zou Lu, Wang Zhengting, and the athletic delegation. Prominent figures from the German government and public were invited to participate in the fellowship. More than 500 people attended.陶鵬飛, the chairman of the student association, delivered a welcome speech, followed by speeches from Ambassador Cheng, President Dai, and the renowned German professor Franke. Finally, the martial arts team gave a performance, and Ms. Yong Zhujun and Mr. Wang Jizhou performed the Chinese opera "Wang Baochuan," concluding the evening with joy late into the night. Now, the original text of the speeches by Mr. Cheng and Mr. Dai are attached to the end of this dispatch.

Speech by Ambassador Cheng

Chairman, ladies and gentlemen, today the Chinese Students Association in Germany is holding a meeting to welcome Mr. Dai Jitao, Mr. Zou Haibin, Mr. Wang Rutang, and the staff of the World Games delegation. We are very pleased and honored to have German guests grace us with their presence.

This is the eleventh World Games, but the first time it has been held in Berlin. Its scale, the thoroughness of its preparation, and the number of participating units and athletes all exceed those of previous Games. The meticulous hospitality extended to athletes from various countries at the Olympic Village is evident, demonstrating the German government and people's emphasis on physical education and their dedication to their work, which is highly admired by foreign visitors. China is participating in the World Games for the third time, but in the eighth Games, there were only staff members, and in the tenth Games, only one athlete was sent. These previous instances were more of an observer-like nature. This year, there are 70 male and female athletes, 27 staff members, 9 martial arts performers, and 36 athletic observers, totaling 142 people. The chief delegate is former Foreign Minister Mr. Wang Rutang, and the National Government has specially appointed President Dai Tao to participate, demonstrating the importance of the event. This is unprecedented. Since the establishment of the new Sino-German treaty in 1921, diplomatic relations have been very harmonious. Now that the World Games are being held in Berlin, China's large-scale official participation further expresses our goodwill towards Germany. In recent years, Germany has shown a vigorous new spirit in every aspect, and in China, the New Life Movement promoted by President Chiang has spread throughout the country. The two countries, East and West, echo each other. After the Chinese delegation arrives in Germany, it will surely gain a deep understanding of Germany's new atmosphere on the sports field, in the dormitories, and at all public gatherings. The German people will also gain an understanding of the new life in China through the arrival of the Chinese delegation. Tianfang firmly believes that through this meeting, the people of the two countries will be able to understand each other better, and the friendship between the two countries will become even more amicable.

Having suffered the pain of the World War, we deeply hate and abhor war and think about how to eliminate it. However, some psychologists say that competition is human nature, so unless this nature is changed, war may not be avoidable. Tianfang believes that competition is indeed human nature, but we can find ways to make it go through the right channels without resorting to war. Sports events are the best form of competition. Participants compete fairly under established rules, which not only does not harm friendship but also enhances feelings. The Chinese philosopher Confucius explained this principle, saying, "The gentleman does not contend for anything except in archery." Modern sports events can also be said to be the competition of gentlemen. If we can only engage in the competition of gentlemen and abandon the barbaric and cruel war, then world peace can be maintained forever.

Mr. Dai Jitao is the first president of National Sun Yat-sen University, and Mr. Zou Haibin is the current president of National Sun Yat-sen University. This university is not only the largest university in China but also has a very deep relationship with Germany. Mr. Dai and Mr. Zou have always admired the development of German science, so National Sun Yat-sen University has hired many German professors over the years, which can be regarded as an organization to communicate Sino-German culture. This is enough to comfort German friends, and makes our welcome to Mr. Dai and Mr. Zou even more meaningful.

I wish Sino-German friendship a limitless future, and wish you all good health.

Speech by President Dai

Tonight, it is a great pleasure to gather with hundreds of compatriots in Berlin, especially with hundreds of strong and enthusiastic athletes and eager and diligent young students, and to have the most cordial fellowship with dignitaries from all walks of life in Germany. This is not only my personal joy, but I also deeply believe that when this great sincerity and loving spirit is transmitted to China, hundreds of millions of people across the country will be stirred up and cheer for it.

The Republic of China, which takes the Three Principles of the People as its highest principle, is gradually building a solid and firm foundation under the cultivation of sincerity, wisdom, benevolence, courage, and virtue. Our purpose is only to follow the teachings of Dr. Sun Yat-sen that "the world belongs to everyone," to build a rich, strong, and peaceful country, and to advance the world to great unity. Since the death of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, Mr. Chiang has led the nation in fighting for this cause for ten years as if it were one day. Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, all central measures have also been for this purpose. This time, with the spirit of national unity, we have organized the athletic delegation and the observation group to come to Berlin to participate in the World Games. Our purpose is not only to gain the benefits of observation in sports but also to seek the effect of mutual learning in the entire culture. The great spirit of the German people and the great achievements they have made are even more worthy of our reference. I believe that after the athletes and observers of our country who participated in the World Games return to the country, their contribution to the country and the world will create a most glorious achievement in the history of Chinese nation-building, and the cultural friendship between the people of China and Germany will be further strengthened. I wish you all good health. (Sent from Berlin on July 28)

(IV)(I) Berlin Before the Opening of the Games

Letters from Berlin to China are sent twice a week. Airmail is sent on Mondays and Fridays, and the Siberian Express is sent on Tuesdays and Fridays. I am rushing to send another report to the country. It is the eve of the opening of the Eleventh World Games.

The entire city of Berlin is truly in a state of frenzy for this event. Wherever you go, you see the symbols of the Games. Whoever you meet, the conversation is always about the Games. The population of Berlin was originally only four million, but this time, the number of people coming from all over the world to participate or visit the Games has reached eight million, more than double the original population. As a result, the prosperous city of Berlin has become even more lively and crowded.

The city administration of Berlin was originally at the forefront among the world's major cities. This time, to improve the city's appearance, all the buildings have been whitewashed and completely renovated, making them even cleaner and more orderly. Except for the occasional fallen and withered leaves on the roads, it is truly spotless. All institutions, shops, and residences are hung with the red-bottomed white-circled "卍" flag and the white-bottomed five-ring Games flag. The flags in front of the larger buildings are five or six zhang long and flutter in the wind, showing the spirit of the event and filling the entire city of Berlin with a warm and tense atmosphere.

The competition venue, the Olympic New Village, and the front of the women's dormitory are filled with spectators every day. Whenever foreigners from any country come out, whether you are an athlete, a staff member, or a journalist, many people will surround you, take photos of you, and ask you to sign autographs. This is also the case when walking on the street. Even many seven- or eight-year-old children are holding a commemorative booklet and a pencil, pulling people to sign autographs. Their innocent and naive look is truly lovely. The enthusiasm of the Germans for the Games can also be seen from this point.

On the 29th, the German boxer Max Schmaling visited the Olympic New Village. As soon as he entered the gate, he was surrounded by hundreds of boxing fans. All the cameras were focused on him. Since defeating the American "Black Bomber" Joe Louis, Schmaling has become a German national hero. When the news of his victory was transmitted from the United States to Germany, German leader Hitler and Minister of Propaganda Goebbels sent congratulatory telegrams. When he returned to Germany from the United States, he was even more warmly welcomed. The Berlin cinemas are showing the film of his match with Joe Louis, and it has not stopped until now. American aviator Colonel Lindbergh, who lives in London, has also come to Berlin to visit the Games. Like Schmaling, he has become a topic of conversation for the public.

All the arrangements for the Games have been completed and are just waiting for the official opening tomorrow afternoon. The order and organization of the Germans are truly admirable. We can describe them in eight words: "No one is idle, and nothing is unattended." Wherever we are, we will never see people wearing badges who are not doing anything. No matter what happens, we will never fail to find someone to take care of it. Therefore, although athletes, staff members, and journalists from various countries have come to a place where they are unfamiliar with the people and the environment, they do not feel any difficulties.

There are a total of 1,200 journalists from various countries who have come specifically for the Games. Among them, there are 72 from Japan, 27 of whom have been officially recognized. The Games has set up a news department to provide news to journalists from various countries. The news department has a large office, and each country has a table and a typewriter for sending out dispatches and writing articles. The table is decorated with the national flags of various countries, and the order is very good. The journalists' seating in the competition venue is located in the best part of the venue. In front of the seats, there is also a long table for placing typewriters, installing telephones, and post offices are also attached to the back. Everything possible that journalists need has been arranged perfectly. Many wireless broadcasting machines have been installed in each sports venue so that representatives from various countries can broadcast news to their own countries. There are more than 400 broadcasting machines in total, and there are more than 1,000 people working on them. From the Chinese side, the journalists are responsible for broadcasting for 20 minutes every day starting at 12:00 noon. Sports programs related to China can also be broadcasted at any time during the competition. The sophistication of the equipment is also impeccable. German Minister of Propaganda Dr. Goebbels hosted a reception for representatives and journalists from various countries in the hall of the German Zoo at 8:00 PM on the 30th. More than 1,000 people attended. It was truly a grand banquet. Those participating from the Chinese side included Chief Delegate Wang Zhengyan, Chief Secretary Shen Siliang, Chu Anping from the Central Daily News, and four journalists. Bands were set up at both ends of the hall, playing melodious tunes at any time. The journalists who participated, although dressed in evening gowns, still could not get rid of their original hippie smiles. Everyone, regardless of nationality or whether they could communicate in the same language, shook hands and talked when they met, filling the great hall with a harmonious and intimate atmosphere. The banquet was very simple, with one soup and two dishes, and snacks and ice cream, unlike the extreme extravagance of the Chinese. After taking their seats, German Central Government Secretary Funk delivered a speech, followed by a speech by World Games President Counlde Bailet Latour. As the banquet was coming to an end, Goebbels stood up in the silence of the entire hall to deliver a speech. The bright lights shone like daylight. Movie cameras and cameras were aimed at him and started working. Although we could not understand the original meaning of his speech, this 38-year-old young politician had a sincere and calm attitude and eloquent speech. The applause from the entire hall was deafening. It is no accident that he is one of Hitler's right-hand men, along with General Goering. Finally, Victor Boin, president of the International Sports Journalists Association, delivered a reply. Because every speech had to be translated into German, English, and French, it was already midnight when everyone walked out of the hall with smiles on their faces.

This Year's Western Soccer League is Divided into Three Groups: A, B, and C. A Reserve Group and a Sunday Morning League are Also Established. Registration for this Year Closes on September 5th 150

The Western Soccer League of this city issued a letter to all member teams yesterday, notifying them of the nine resolutions passed by the Executive Committee of the League. These resolutions will be implemented this season, with several terms being from 1937 to 1938. If member teams have any proposals or are unclear about the resolutions, they can send a letter to the secretariat of the League for inquiries before September 3rd. This year's registration will close on September 5th. The relevant resolutions are as follows:

(1) This year's Shanghai Western Soccer League is divided into three groups (Groups A, B, and C). (2) There is also a reserve group, which is specifically for reserve teams to join Group A. Players in the reserve group are not restricted from competing in Group A. (3) Member teams that join Group A must join a reserve group team. (4) The last-placed team in Group A must be relegated to Group B, and the champion of Group B can be promoted to Group A (but must join a reserve group team). The last-placed team in Group B is relegated to Group C, and the champion of Group C can be promoted to Group B. (5) A Sunday Morning League is prepared to replace last year's Group E, limited to twelve teams. (6) All member teams can join the League or the Sunday Morning League. (7) Each member team can join at most "teams in the League or the Sunday Morning League. (8) In each competition, the winner gets two points, the loser gets zero points, and a tie gets one point each. If the scores are the same after the end, the average goal is used to determine the winner. (9) This season's League Committee will consist of five people, three of whom will be selected from the Executive Committee, and the remaining two will be selected from the various member teams. This committee has no administrative power, but can report to the Executive Committee for handling. Please note the supplementary rules. Registration will close around September 5th.

In yesterday's two senior baseball league games, McBain Second League defeated McBain First League by twelve to six, while Amateur defeated China by seven to zero. The first cycle has now ended, and the results are as follows:

Hitler Visits the Venue

Education News

The Second Day of the Joint Annual Meeting of Seven Scientific Societies: Experts from Various Societies Have New Inventions. Chang-ying Zhang et al. Invented that Hamsters Can Reproduce in the Laboratory. De-jun Yu et al. Invented New Species and Varieties of Rosaceae Plants in China. Zhao-lun Zeng Used the Pirani Method to Determine Phosphorus and Bismuth in Organic Matter. 152

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) The Chinese Science Society, Zoological Society, Botanical Society, Physical Society, Chemical Society, Mathematical Society, and Geographical Society, seven scientific organizations, held sessions at Tsinghua and Yenching Universities this morning (18th) to read papers and present inventions, resulting in numerous discoveries. In the afternoon, each society held business meetings. The Chinese Science Society proposed an amendment to the current calendar. On the 20th, the seven scientific organizations will jointly discuss the matter again. Details from various fields are recorded as follows: The Zoological Society convened at 8 a.m. in the auditorium of the Tsinghua Biological Hall to read papers. Among the inventions was "Hamsters Raised in the Laboratory Can Reproduce," by Xian Wu and Chang-ying Zhang. The key points of the invention are as follows: In 1919, En-zeng Xie used hamsters in medical experiments to replace white mice. Since then, the use of hamsters in experiments has been frequently reported, but no one has been able to make them reproduce in the laboratory. The main reason why hamsters cannot reproduce in the laboratory is that the female hamsters have irregular periods. If ovarian extract is added to the diet of female hamsters daily, their periods can be regulated after one month. Detailed observations were made on the daily height, weight, and physical development of hamsters during their growth period.

New Botanical Inventions

The Botanical Society convened at 8 a.m. in the Tsinghua Chemistry Building to read papers. The new inventions are recorded as follows: (1) Jing-yue Zhang read a paper on "The Growth and Differentiation of Soybean Stems and Leaves under Different Light Intensities." The main points of the invention are as follows: (1) The lower the light intensity, the longer the internodes and the greater the growth rate. (2) When the light intensity decreases, the leaves (leaf blades and petioles) become smaller, and the growth gradually slows down. (3) When the light intensity decreases, the differentiation rate of the stem tip also decreases. (4) When the light is very weak, the stem elongates extremely quickly, but the plant dies soon after. (5) Plants moved from strong light to a dark room grow less in the dark room the more they are exposed to light beforehand. (6) If only the tip of the plant is covered with black paper, the stems and leaves continue to grow very quickly. (2) De-jun Yu and Xi-tao Cai read a paper on "Rosaceae Plants in China." As a result of their research, they discovered two new species and two new varieties of Chinese roses, recorded as follows: Bosa bella Rehdet wib var nudayu et tsai (new variety). This variety differs from the original species in that its flowers are smaller and have smooth receptacles and pedicels. It is distributed in Shaanxi and Henan. (2) Rosa kwangtungensis yu et tsai (new species). This species is common in Guangdong. Most botanists previously mistakenly identified it as R. multifloa tbunberg, but it differs from the latter in that it has pubescent styles and stipules that are not pectinate. Some considered it a close relative of R. souliana crepin, which is produced in southwestern China, but it differs from the latter in that it is entirely covered with gray pubescence and is distributed in Guangdong. (3) Rosa lioui yu et tsai (new species). This new species belongs to the Cinnamomeae tribe and is a close relative of Rlaxa rety and R. Beggeriana schernk. It differs from the two in that the curved thorns under its stipules are large and shiny, and its bracts are narrowly lanceolate or linear-lanceolate, and its pedicels and receptacles are tightly covered with short hairs. It is distributed in Xinjiang. (4) Rosa moyesii var pubscens yu et tsai (new variety). This variety differs from the original species in that it has spines as long as the leaflets, the bases of the spines are enlarged, and the rachis and the underside of the leaflets have dense short hairs. It is distributed in Xikang.

New Chemical Inventions

The Chemical Society convened at 8 a.m. in the Yenching Chemistry Building to read papers. The inventions are recorded in the following order: (1) Zhao-lun Zeng read a paper on "The Determination of Phosphorus, Bismuth, Silicon, and Boron in Organic Compounds Using the Pirani Method." The key points of the invention are as follows: The Pirani method is now the simplest method for determining organic sulfur and halogens. Previous researchers have also tried to use this method to determine other elements. The author has now subjected organic compounds containing phosphorus, bismuth, silicon, and boron to Pirani melting (using sodium peroxide), then dissolved them in water, and applied the methods used in ordinary inorganic analysis to determine these elements. As a result, except for the analysis of boron, which was relatively poor, the rest can be considered satisfactory. (2) Yun-pu Liu read a paper on "A Variant of the Rast Micro-determination Method for Molecular Weight." The key points of the invention are as follows: To improve the usability and accuracy, the variant of the Rast micro-determination method for molecular weight was modified again. A melting point determination bulb was used instead of a melting point measurement tube. The test results obtained were satisfactory. The percentage difference of the molecular weight determined for each of the twenty different items was smaller than that of all previous researchers.

New Geographical Inventions

The Geographical Society convened at 8 a.m. in the Tsinghua Science Lecture Hall to read papers. Fu-ti Yuan read a paper on "The Lower and Middle Mesozoic Strata in Xinjiang." He discovered the lower Mesozoic strata in Shuixi Valley, Fuyuan County, and discovered fish fossils in the Triassic strata near Dihua. The newly discovered points are recorded as follows: In May of the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, when I (Yuan) was investigating the geology of Xinjiang, I discovered the lower Mesozoic strata in Shuixi Valley, Fuyuan County, and learned that its coal and iron were all in sedimentary rocks, mostly Jurassic. However, I discovered several more rock layers below it, so I continued to pursue them. In September of the same year, I discovered fossils of therapsid reptiles in the Triassic strata. In the eighteenth and nineteenth years, I continued to excavate in Fuyuan, Fukang, and Qitai counties. In the twentieth year, I discovered fish fossils in the Triassic strata near Dihua. I discovered seven locations rich in reptile fossils in the northern Tianshan Mountains and collected nearly seventy specimens in total. The work period extended to the summer of the twentieth year, but all the time was spent on preliminary collection work. All of my collected items were transported to Beiping with me in May of the eleventh year. Mr. Zhong-jian Yang gladly accepted to identify the reptile fossils. In the twenty-third year, the paleobotanist Mr. Xing-jian Si and Mr. Jun-ding Ge identified plant fossils and Triassic fish fossils, respectively. Therefore, my geological work in the northern Tianshan Mountains, according to the geological age indicated by the fossils, was able to be determined in detail. Repairing the fossils also took a lot of time. In the past three years, under the supervision of Mr. Yang, eight reptile fossils have been repaired, belonging to three orders, five genera, six classes, and two different periods. If environmental conditions permit, I will continue to sort out the remaining sixty specimens, and there may be new materials discovered.

Ultra-High Frequency Radio Waves

From 4 to 5 p.m., the joint annual meeting held a public lecture in the Tsinghua Science Museum. Zhi-gong Ren spoke on "The Effects of Ultra-High Frequency Radio Waves on Living Organisms," briefly stating that we have long known that R-rays, X-rays, and ultraviolet rays, which belong to electromagnetic waves, have special effects on living organisms. High-frequency radio waves are also a band of the electromagnetic spectrum and have even more significant effects on living organisms, especially ultra-high frequencies. This type of ultra-high frequency wave can be generated by a vacuum tube oscillator. The capacitor of the oscillator has a high-frequency electric field, and its coil has a high magnetic field. If we place a living organism in a high-frequency electric or magnetic field, the most noticeable phenomenon is the rapid increase in the organism's temperature, the speed of which depends on the strength of the field, the type and size of the organism, and its health condition. We have experimented with a variety of organisms. Warm-blooded animals include white mice, guinea pigs, rabbits, cats, dogs, sparrows, and pigeons. Cold-blooded animals include frogs, tadpoles, toads, fish, bees, and fruit flies. If they are subjected to a high-frequency electric field, they will die after a considerable period of time (ranging from one to eighty minutes). However, if they are subjected to a high-frequency magnetic field, warm-blooded animals die in much the same way, while cold-blooded animals show no significant effects after several hours. According to the results of our autopsies on dead organisms, all organisms that die from high-frequency field forces die from increased heat. Other effects may also exist simultaneously, but because the heating effect is so great, it overshadows everything, and we cannot easily detect them for the time being. We have tried to adopt Debye's theory for electrolytes and liquids. Debye believed that the conductivity of electrolytes or polar liquids must change depending on the frequency. As the frequency increases from low to high, the conductivity also increases, until it increases particularly at ultra-high frequencies. As a result, the ability to absorb electrical energy is also particularly great. The effect of ultra-high frequency waves to heat the inside of living organisms has now been practically applied to the treatment of many diseases and is a very useful new development for medicine.

Special Article: A Comparison of Silk Production and Sales in China and Japan in the Last Ten Years 168

—He Yan

Silk is one of China's important agricultural products, and its prosperity or decline has a huge impact on the domestic rural economy and urban prosperity. However, because China, which has a history of more than 2,000 years of sericulture and silk production, has seen technological and economic improvements in silk-producing countries such as Japan and Italy in modern times, and the government authorities have provided effective assistance, the production and sales of their silk have been making great strides. Japanese raw silk has even grasped the hegemony of manipulating raw silk trade in the world market, and it is almost possible to monopolize it. (Japanese silk accounts for about 98% of all silk imported by the United States, which accounts for 70% of the world's total raw silk consumption.) Looking back at China, in recent years, the silk industry has been working hard to improve products, and there is no shortage of people, but those that have been implemented and have achieved results are still in the budding and promotion stages. As for those who only care about temporary and personal interests, and cause Chinese silk to lose its reputation abroad, there are many people. (This point refers to Chinese speculative silk merchants and irregular export foreign merchants, such as those who buy inferior silk products, change silk labels, and abuse the upgrade to sell to foreign countries at high prices.) Both of these combined, the situation of their panting under the threat of Japanese silk is exactly the same, and the fact that they still cannot have rapid and reasonable improvement is also the same. Here is a table of the raw silk production of China, Japan, and Italy in the past eleven years to see how the raw silk of each country is affected by its environment (political, economic, scientific) differently, and how it affects its production.

Raw Silk Production in Various Countries in the Past Eleven Years (Unit: 1,000 pounds)

(The statistics in this table are based on the figures published by the National Textile Manufacturers Association of America)

Judging from the numbers in the above table, the average annual output of Japanese silk accounts for 75% of the world's total output. From 1923 to 1930, China's raw silk production showed a gradual increase every year. However, since 1931, it has suddenly decreased. Although there was a slight increase again in 1933, it declined again in 1934. (It is estimated that in 1931, it decreased by 1,577,000 pounds compared with the previous year, and in 1932, it dropped sharply to only 9,023,000 pounds. Although it increased to 10,820,000 pounds in 1933, it only produced 8,805,000 pounds in the following year, only four-tenths of the production in 1929.) The astonishing sharp decline, compared with the annual increase in Japanese silk production, is even more inferior. (To be continued)
