Recently, because there are only a few days left in this month, major factories still need to raise funds, so it can already be drawn at the same price.

Wheat Futures Followed the Decline by 67 Fen 170

Yesterday's wheat futures market showed a state of initially being flat and then plummeting after the opening in the morning. When the price was opened, people were already mainly stable because the quoted price of foreign wheat was still slightly rising, so the opening price was similar to the previous day. As it approached the second session and below, some bulls tended to sell off because the decline in the flour market was very strong, and the opening price was immediately lower. Originally, the market sentiment had no fixed purpose. If there were more buyers, they would follow in, and vice versa, they would compete to sell, and it often did not match the actual distance. The opening price for this month was 5.08 yuan, and the closing price was only 1 fen, with a difference of 7 fen. The others also reached 67 fen each. The market has already reached such a high level. If the flour sales become sluggish, a reversal must be prevented. Spot wheat market, due to the sharp decline in standards and the suspension of factory purchases, all brokers shouted Xiao Wu Fen to open Baluling Linhuai Pass at 5.05 yuan, then to 0.03 yuan, Bengbu wheat at 5.01 yuan, then 4.99 yuan, Zhuzhen wheat at 5.01 yuan, Gaoyou wheat at 4.97 yuan, then 9.5 jiao, Dongtai Daqiao wheat at 4.95 yuan, Shaoxing wheat at 4.79 yuan. Fuxin bought 4,000 packages.

White Japonica and Thin Rice Sales Are Both Dull 171

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, a total of 17 or 18 shipments arrived from various gangs, totaling 3,400 or 500 stones, most of which were thin rice. Therefore, although 6700 packages were handled by the Dalian Qingdao Qinhuangdao gangs in the thin rice market, the result was still a reduction of 12 jiao or more. The price of thick early japonica rice depreciated by a few fen due to the sluggish sales in this street market. Du Yangjian was in short supply and the price was stable. Yinyuan rice was similar. A total of more than 1,500 stones arrived in Dongxin, and the route was flat, falling by 2 chi.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 356 boats arrived from various routes in Hexia. The various types of white japonica Yang Dufu Kejian were very dull in the market. The sales of thin rice Bianyuan and Lianhao were slightly better. The market price of high-quality white japonica was barely stable, while the medium and inferior ones were about 1 jiao lower. The price of Bianyuan thin rice fell by about 1 jiao. The various indica rices were weak by a few fen. The supply of Dongxin was quite abundant, but the sales were sluggish, and the price was slightly lower by 2 jiao.

Rough Indica Rice Sells Well and Rises Sharply 172

Yesterday's market situation for customer indica rice was such that arrivals and sales were both strong, and the market atmosphere remained active. However, after the various stalls of machine-milled white rice had jumped in price the day before yesterday, the customers this time were not as greedy as they were a few days ago. The price of rough rice, on the other hand, had fallen sharply by 23 jiao previously, and the degree of decline was too high, which in turn triggered the customers to continue to buy. Therefore, the machine-milled rice has temporarily stabilized, while the rough rice has risen sharply by more than 1.5 jiao. The main route is still this street, and the Ningbo gang, Shantou, Xiamen, inland, and northern ports are all embellishments. 3,500 packages of Hankou goods, 2,480 packages of Jiangxi rice, 100 packages of Hunan rice, and 290 packages of Taiwan rice were offered for rough rice.

The Rising Trend of New Sesame Seeds Has Subsided, and New Soybeans Have No Ups and Downs for the Time Being 173

The rising trend of new sesame seeds from foreign firms has temporarily subsided. Because foreign merchants are hindered by the continuously rising prices and do not intend to buy, the market atmosphere has been flattened. Yesterday, only Jardine Matheson dumped 200 tons at a price of 12.8 yuan, with delivery scheduled for October and November. The future trend mainly depends on the thickness of the route. The new soybeans are hovering, and the high-quality goods are tight, due to the consecutive purchases by oil mills and the inquiries from the Fuzhou gang. Therefore, the overall situation has no ups and downs for the time being. It is estimated that more than 50 packages of various new beans were opened yesterday.

Seafood: New Crop of Grade 10 Sea Cucumber and Dried Scallops are Scarce, So Market Prices are Exceptionally Firm 174

The new crop of Grade 10 sea cucumber is scarce this year, and the source is very rare. Therefore, the market price has peaked, and there is often a shortage of goods to supply the market. Yesterday, brokerage firms offered 14 boxes of new Jiang Co sea cucumber, estimated at 38 pieces at 298 yuan, 45 pieces at 282 yuan, 50 pieces at 277 yuan, 60 pieces at 261.5 yuan, and 75 pieces at 244 yuan. The brokers' appetite for importing is strong, and the goods are cleared as they arrive. The market situation is exceptionally firm.

According to news from the producing area of dried scallops, the production of new goods is not high. The cost of shipping to Shanghai based on the local price is estimated to be more than 170 yuan. Therefore, the selling price of the old goods stored in this city's streets is tightening. The current selling price of brokers is quoted at 167 yuan for medium-sized Qiushui goods. The market is expected to rise further.

Dried and Preserved Goods: Hainan Longan Drops by 12 Yuan 175

The arrival of Hainan longan has increased slightly this time. Because sales are gradually becoming flat, sentiment is softening. Yesterday, it was heard that the various stores in the north-south market opened a total of one hundred and dozens of pieces, a decrease of 12 yuan compared to before. If more goods arrive in the next batch, the opening price may continue to loosen, because Guangzhou longan has also dropped significantly.

Popular Lecture

Li Yuexun 189

— Ji Zhen

When the law loses its function, virtuous men are compelled to take matters into their own hands, acting on the principle of "drawing their swords when injustice is seen on the road."

During the Qianlong era of the Qing dynasty, there was a poor scholar in Zhangnan named Li Yuexun. From a young age, he was known for his moral character and diligence in learning, earning the respect of the entire village. At that time, the eight-legged essay was the only path for scholars. Yuexun became a Xiucai (a degree in the imperial examination system) at the age of sixteen, and he happily thought, "The villagers value me so much, I must do great things for them. I passed the Xiucai exam at such a young age, if I continue to work hard, passing the Juren and Jinshi exams will not be difficult. Once the path of the imperial examination is open, I can become a high-ranking official and do public good for the village!" Who knew that after reading the eight-legged essay for two more years and gaining a deeper understanding of worldly affairs, doubts arose in his heart. He often asked himself, "If I want to do something truly practical for the people, I should seek practical knowledge. If I want to reform society, I should understand society; if I want to understand society, I should read more history. Zizhuang often has water troubles, if I want to relieve the suffering of the villagers, I should study water conservancy. Other things like studying military affairs, promoting agriculture, studying engineering, studying commerce, etc., are all practical knowledge, but the eight-legged essay completely ignores these. If I only focus on the eight-legged essay today, even if I am lucky enough to become famous and a high-ranking official in the future, what will I rely on to govern the world and benefit the people?..."

He thought about abandoning the eight-legged essay, hesitated for a long time, unable to make a decision. He still followed the routine of reading the eight-legged essay and taking the exams. One day, his wife fell ill from hunger. He was very anxious and wanted to borrow a liter of beans to cook porridge for her, but he ran into obstacles everywhere all day long, returning empty-handed at dusk. He felt ashamed and lingered outside the door, not daring to go inside to see his wife. But he was afraid that she would really starve to death, so he became anxious again. With his hands behind his back, he knelt and peered through the crack in the door. It was already time to light the lamps, but the room was pitch black, and he couldn't see anything. Just as he was racking his brains for a solution, someone unexpectedly and quietly placed a pile of things in his hand. When he turned around to look, he only saw a small shadow dart into the house next door on the left. In the dim twilight, he could still clearly see that what he held in his hands were five white cakes. Remembering many similar experiences in the past, he immediately knew what was going on this time. It turned out that there was a child selling cakes next door who felt sorry for him not having food and often reheated leftover cakes and sent them to him. This child was very clever, he knew that scholars valued their reputation the most, so he always quietly delivered the cakes, dropping them off and running away. Yuexun would not accept them unless he was really starving. Often, the child would quietly send the cakes, and Yuexun would ask his wife to quietly send them back. This time, in order to save his wife who was about to starve to death, he couldn't insist on that anymore. He felt as if he had received a million gold, happily holding the cakes and pushing the door open. He relied on those few cakes to save his wife's life.

When his wife recovered her strength, she said to Yuexun, "Look, even a child who sells cakes can support a family and help others. You are a man who stands tall and firm, but you have only read a few dead books, unable to handle light or heavy tasks, and you can't even support yourself. I think the eight-legged essay is harmful, let's not study it anymore. It is more proper to honestly farm the land or do business. Although it is said that passing the imperial examination can lead to becoming an official, didn't you say that you don't want to become an official, but want to save people? If you can't save yourself, how can you save others? I don't believe that a person is useless before passing the examination, and becomes capable after passing it. Don't deceive yourself! You should open your eyes and see what the current dignitaries are like. Aren't they all from the imperial examination? What have they actually done? This is not the way, you should give up."

After hearing his wife's words, Yuexun decided to give up the eight-legged essay and farm the land to support his family. In his spare time, he read more practical books, and his knowledge improved day by day. But unfortunately, the country had established the system of selecting officials through the imperial examination, and Yuexun lacked this stepping stone of the eight-legged essay, so he was never recognized for his talent in his life. The method of selecting scholars was flawed, and the appointment of people was inappropriate, causing the common people to suffer countless losses. Although the country had laws to protect the public, "the heavens are high and the emperor is far away," and the oppressed common people, unable to see the light of day due to the power of the authorities, had no way to appeal. Yuexun was a benevolent person full of love for the world, and he couldn't bear to see injustice. He often drew his sword when he saw injustice on the road, doing many good deeds of eliminating evil and helping the good in the village, so everyone called him Li the Swordsman. He often sighed to people, "The gentlemen of ancient times were deeply concerned about the people, so they aspired to be good doctors even if they couldn't be good ministers. Today, I can't bear to see people suffer losses, unable to enforce the law, so I can only act as a knight-errant. Alas, how could this be my original intention—I want to save the people of the world from deep water and scorching fire. When I hear someone crying from hunger and cold, I feel it is my responsibility, but what can a knight-errant accomplish? Those who don't know me may think that I enjoy being a knight-errant, but in fact, this is my inevitable and unavoidable behavior!"

The people of Zizhuang knew that Yuexun could protect the weak and seek justice for the wronged, so whoever suffered injustice would go to Yuexun. Yuexun often wore short clothes and trousers, carrying two knives when he traveled, his imposing manner intimidating, causing even the bullies to lose their courage. Yuexun did many remarkable things in the village, but his rescue of a certain widow was the most touching.

There was a young and beautiful widow in Zizhuang, living with her fourteen-year-old son and refusing to remarry. Her younger brother-in-law, greedy for the money of Hou Liu from Nei Huang, secretly sold his sister-in-law to him. When the wedding sedan came to pick her up, the younger brother-in-law ordered the people to hide in the nearby ancient temple first, and then he went home to trick his sister-in-law out under a pretext. As soon as she came out, the dozens of people hiding in the temple also ran out. She didn't know what was going on, and was shocked. She turned around to go home, but the gate was already tightly closed. With nowhere to go, the wedding party seized the opportunity to grab her, forcibly put her in the sedan, and escorted her away. Her son heard the unfortunate news and rushed to rescue her, but it was too late. He knew that he couldn't win against the crowd, and chasing after them would only be a futile death. He wouldn't be able to get her back. So he ran to find Yuexun, running before Yuexun and crying for help. Yuexun frowned and said, "This matter is not easy to handle! That Hou Liu is a brave warrior, and your mother is already in his hands. The journey is far, I'm afraid we won't be able to get her back in time." The widow's son, hearing Yuexun's words, knelt down desperately, refusing to get up, and cried even more bitterly. Yuexun couldn't bear it, so he agreed generously, "Rescuing your mother is indeed my responsibility, I will go immediately. If I can't get your mother back, I will not return alive." After Yuexun finished speaking, he came out and gathered his followers, saying, "In the village, I have always been known for my chivalry. Today, someone has robbed a woman in our village, and if I can't save her, what kind of chivalry am I? I originally wanted to file a lawsuit for her, but the officials these days are all bastards, they only know how to be greedy and accept bribes, how can they handle anything? Moreover, the documents have to go through the province and the checkpoints, it will take several months to move, how can we make it in time? That Hou Liu, seeing that we are pressing him urgently, will immediately get married. If the woman is married to him, what's the point of asking her to come back? Then, even if the lawsuit is won, it will be like a loss, what's the use? I think it's better to use force to rob Hou Liu alive. Even if we can't get the woman, capturing Hou Liu can still protect her." Everyone listened to Yuexun's words and agreed. Yuexun then selected twenty-seven people to go with him.

Hou Liu lived in Gangu, twenty li away from Zizhuang. Yuexun led his men and arrived there late at night. Finding Hou Liu's house, he directed his followers to push open the door and go straight into the hall. At that time, the guests were all seated, and everyone was unguarded, drinking happily. Suddenly seeing Yuexun and his men rushing in with swords, everyone was shocked. They wanted to besiege Yuexun and others, but they were unarmed and didn't know what to do. Yuexun opened his eyes wide and shouted loudly, scaring them all back. They trampled on each other, extremely embarrassed, and had no other way. Yuexun seized the opportunity to run into the bride's room to find the woman. At that time, Hou Liu had already hidden the woman in the straw hut and was looking for people to help him resist Yuexun. Unexpectedly, before he was ready, Yuexun had already arrived. Yuexun tightly grabbed Hou Liu's wrist with his left hand, pulled out the knife at his waist to threaten him, and loudly rebuked, "Haven't you heard of Li Yuexun in Zizhuang? How dare you come to my village to rob a woman? Where is the woman now? Hand her over quickly, or I will kill you." Hou Liu answered in a trembling voice, "I, I, I have already released her." Yuexun knew that Hou Liu was lying to him, and angrily ordered his men to tie Hou Liu's hands behind his back. As soon as they were tied up, the young people in the village, not knowing the details, heard that there were violent intruders in the Hou family, and rushed to attack Yuexun with weapons. Seeing the menacing momentum, Yuexun knew that he could only win by relying on both wisdom and courage, so he ordered his twenty-seven men to stand guard with their weapons facing outward, while he stood in the middle, holding his knife against Hou Liu's neck, and said to the crowd in a stern voice, "Yuexun has come this time with no intention of returning alive. Those who dare to fight me, come on!" As he spoke, he raised his knife and tested it on Hou Liu's neck, implying, "If you make any move, I will kill him first." The crowd, seeing this terrifying scene, were all sweating with fear, standing far away, not daring to approach. Yuexun asked Hou Liu again, "Where is the woman?" Hou Liu refused to tell the truth, Yuexun was angry, and dragged Hou Liu out. Before he reached the door, he heard the woman's crying. Yuexun and others followed the sound and found her in the straw hut. So Yuexun ordered the twenty-seven men to protect her and walk ahead, while he drove Hou Liu behind him with his knife. The people of Gangu were afraid of Yuexun, and no one dared to chase after him. Seeing that he had completely won, Yuexun didn't want to overuse his power. He released Hou Liu halfway and said to him, "Li Yuexun of Zizhuang is not afraid of death. If you want revenge, I will be waiting for you at home tomorrow." Hou Liu mumbled and dared not say anything. As soon as he was free, he fled as if escaping from the tiger's mouth.

Late at night, Yuexun returned to Zizhuang, handed the widow over to her son, and then dismissed his men. When the widow's son went to ask Yuexun for help, her younger brother-in-law, fearing Yuexun's reprimand, had already fled. Hou Liu, having learned his lesson, was also afraid and dared not come to feud with Yuexun again. From then on, as long as Yuexun was in Zizhuang, there was peace and tranquility.

Jean-Baptiste Lamarck (1744-1829) 190

— Bao

—A Courageous Naturalist—

Lamarck was born in 1744 in the countryside of Bazentin, Picardy, France. He came from a poor family, his father was a soldier. Lamarck had eleven siblings, he himself was the youngest. Many people in his family joined the army, his three elder brothers were soldiers, and the eldest brother had bravely died in battle during a siege. When Lamarck was very young, he would say to his father, "Elder brother died for the country, how glorious! I want to emulate him, Dad, he will take me with him, won't he?" His father's eyes turned red, unable to speak. But in his heart, he decided that Lamarck should study to be a monk. Soon, he sent him to school in Amiens to study. He reluctantly studied there for a few years, often imagining the heroic life of a soldier when no one was watching, and always wanting to join the army. He repeatedly wrote letters requesting his father, but each time he received a firm rejection. At the age of sixteen, he received the news of his father's death, and immediately left school to rush home for the funeral. The passion of loving his parents and the terror of death made him feel that life was short and he should make an effort in time, preparing for a glorious death. It further strengthened his determination to join the army.

At that time, the Besujolais regiment was fighting in Vestphaha. Lamarck managed to get a letter of introduction and ran there to join the army. The captain saw that he was a child and didn't take him seriously. But out of courtesy, he had to accept him. He could only let him join the ranks. Then, due to the urgency of the war, he no longer paid attention to this little soldier. After a fierce battle at night, many people were killed and wounded on both sides. The next day, everyone transferred troops from the rear to replenish the ranks, and prepared for a big battle. Just after dawn, the captain ran to the front line to command, transferring the soldiers who fought bravely last night to the rear. He suddenly noticed Lamarck and asked in surprise, "Kid, how come you are here too?"

It turned out that last night the captain had handed him over to a platoon leader. The platoon leader was unhappy to have such a small soldier and secretly said to the captain, "Why recruit a child? If you love him, treat him like a treasure, why assign him to my name?" He suddenly had malicious intent out of hatred and said, "Okay, let's just kill him quickly. How much courage does he have? Send him to the front line, without personally engaging in battle, I think he will be scared to death." The platoon leader immediately sent him to the front line where the fighting was taking place. Unexpectedly, he wasn't afraid at all, fighting bravely in the hail of bullets all night. The next day, he still stood bravely on the front line, refusing to retreat. When the captain asked him, he didn't really answer the captain's questions, but insisted on serving on the front line. He finally said to the captain with tears in his eyes, "I come from a military family and have received military training since I was a child. Captain, please believe me, just let me serve on the front line! I can't let my elder brother have all the glory, Captain, you know how gloriously he died!" Just then, the enemy came to challenge again, and the camp sounded the emergency assembly call, preparing for battle. The captain didn't have time to say much, silently agreeing and running to the front line to command. Lamarck assumed that the captain had tacitly approved him, and immediately followed the bugle call to assemble, going to the front line to resist the enemy. This time, France was defeated, almost all the officers were killed in battle, and the soldiers were very panicked, disregarding discipline and scrambling to retreat. Only Lamarck's small team, seeing him fighting bravely, all stayed on the front line and fought desperately against the enemy. Finally, they received the order from the regimental commander, and they guarded the order, covering each other while retreating to the defense line. The captain saw that Lamarck was so loyal and brave, and immediately formally reused him. The war soon ended, and the regiment went to Monaco to be stationed. One day, a newly arrived officer heard people talking about Lamarck's brave and courageous deeds, and was so excited that he lifted Lamarck up by the head. Unexpectedly, he injured his neck, developing a terrible cervical adenitis, forcing him to return to Paris for treatment.

After recovering from his illness, he changed his career to study medicine. But because he was too poor, he had to spend most of his time earning a living. At the same time, he liked to go to the Royal Garden to study plants, reading all the books there about plants. As a result, his progress in medicine was not as good as his botany. Later, he became fond of mathematics and wanted to change his career again, but his brothers advised him to continue studying medicine, which made him even more confused. Fortunately, he met the great French philosopher Rousseau there. Rousseau took him around to collect plants. Influenced by Rousseau, he decided to give up medicine and specialize in botany. His brothers opposed him, but he didn't care. After returning from his travels, he chose botany as a subject under the famous botanist Bernard de Jussieu and studied it carefully.

During his studies, he lived a very hard life. Some wealthy relatives felt sorry for him and often came to persuade him, "Lamarck, with your intelligence, it would be easy to develop in the military, political, or even business world, and gain both fame and fortune. Why suffer like this? It's not easy to become a naturalist. You have been working hard for several years, exhausting yourself, and still haven't achieved any results. This proves that you cannot become a naturalist. Actually, what's so great about being a naturalist? You might as well give up and change your career with me. I can immediately find you a good job."

Lamarck, who was making progress in his research, became angry when he heard such disheartening words and sternly refused, "Thank you for your kindness, but unfortunately, this is not something you can understand. I believe that the most interesting subject in the world is natural history, and the most valuable people are naturalists. I also believe that if I work hard, I will definitely succeed in becoming a naturalist. However, great talents mature late, and the more valuable something is, the higher the price it requires. So I want to devote all my time and energy to pursuing my knowledge. I am even willing to sacrifice my life for it. What does suffering mean?" Seeing him studying so diligently, people stopped bothering him.

At the age of thirty-four, his book Flora Francocie was published, and soon became popular, making him famous. The following year, he was appreciated by the French king and selected as a member of the Academy of Sciences. Later, he was appointed as the administrator of the Royal "Collection of Plants". Although he received high honors, his income was very meager, and he had to support five children. As a result, he still had to live a hard life. Fortunately, he had a spirit of enduring hardship, able to withstand all difficulties, and constantly striving for further study. In 1793, the Paris Museum of Natural History, which Lamarck advocated and founded, was established. Lamarck served as the administrator of the neglected Invertebrate Department, and independently engaged in research. He invented the terms "Vertebrates" and "Invertebrates", which are still in use today. The invertebrates studied by Lamarck had mostly not been discussed by predecessors, and were complex and chaotic. Lamarck spent eight years of effort to sort them out and publish his masterpiece Système des Animaux sans Vertèbres (System of Animals without Vertebrae). Because of his efforts and research achievements, year after year were amazing. In his old age, he gained extremely high prestige, succeeding Linnaeus as the world's great naturalist.

Unified Sales Method for Magazines and Books, and Other Matters 191

— Chen Zhongxian

Since the Ministry of Education promulgated the "Unified Sales Method for Textbooks and Other Books" on April 7th of this year, it seems to have had some impact on the publishing industry. In the 58th issue of this publication, Mr. Duxiu (Chen Duxiu) specially wrote an article as a letter of good news, believing that "this is an unprecedented transformation in the publishing industry" and "the prelude to the great flowering of the entire Chinese cultural world." Indeed, this is a perfect and thorough method! On June 2nd, the Shanghai Booksellers' Association, which holds the key to the national publishing industry, re-established a 15-chapter, 64-article implementation method based on the ministry's outline. Shortly thereafter, the New Life Bookstore and Kaiming Bookstore followed by reducing prices and publishing book catalogs. Such a surge made me secretly happy, thinking that there was great hope for the future. However, upon turning to the June 30th announcement of the Booksellers' Association, unfortunately, this 15-chapter grand plan was postponed for six months due to "cumbersome procedures" and "insufficient preparation." Although the outline issued by the Ministry of Education remains the law and still exists.

However, we must not ignore the outline issued by the Ministry and the methods formulated by the Association simply because the Ministry's methods have had little response or because of the six-month postponement. Moreover, this is indeed a major reform in the publishing industry! Therefore, I am eager to take this opportunity to discuss these two articles, highlighting the key points.

The ten key points of this ministry's decree are: (1) Books must be marked with a fixed price; (2) Textbook prices should be reduced; (3) Books are not allowed to have discounts; (4) Published books must have reduced prices; (5) Pre-orders have a minimum special price of 70%; (6) Stipulate discounts for wholesale purchases by industry libraries, schools, and publishers; (7) Cheap sales or book coupons are not allowed; (8) Slow-selling or damaged books may be sold in a discount section; (9) Outlying areas may add appropriate remittance and freight charges; (10) Those who violate the regulations will be sanctioned.

The failure to mark books with a fixed price is most common in ancient books (thread-bound books). Yuan Dynasty block prints, rare book reprints—these provide publishers with many opportunities to make money. At the same time, readers often spend high prices and do not get good books because they are unfamiliar with the inside story. Furthermore, because fixed prices are not marked, bookstores often determine the price of books based on their capital and the level of profit they want to obtain, thus readers do not know what to do, and the industry competes with each other. Therefore, the Ministry of Education's current regulation of this point is indeed a fundamental solution.

However, ancient books are, after all, not like new books that are published endlessly. Moreover, even after fixed prices are established, they can still be sold at 70% off, 50% off, or even a 7% discount? Therefore, Article 3 of the Ministry of Education stipulates that discounts or price increases are not allowed. In this way, not only do purchasers feel great convenience, but publishers, as the Shanghai Booksellers' Association says, "either raise the fixed price and give large discounts, or create clever names and promote fair prices, causing unfair competition among the industry and leading to unnecessary disputes and losses." This problem can also be avoided at the same time.

However, in order to take into account the facts, the Ministry of Education specifically stipulated Articles 5 and 8 to facilitate the publication of new books and the sale of old books. This cannot be regarded as a thorough consideration of business difficulties; at the same time, it is also a remedial measure that the publishing industry should have. Therefore, in the implementation methods formulated by the Shanghai Booksellers' Association, the methods are specified in detail in Chapters 7, 8, and 9, such as the limit on the number of times per year and the limit on the number of books, as well as the location, time, etc., which are extremely thorough.

In addition, the point about wholesale within the industry is quite noteworthy. In the past, I often had this experience. For example, if Commercial Press published a book, it was sold at the fixed price in the main store, but in other small bookstores, it was often available at a 70% or 80% discount. The purpose of the main store not giving discounts is to maintain its reputation and the strength of its brand, which goes without saying. However, from the 70% or 80% discount at small stores, it can be inferred that the discounts between them are large, no less than 50% or 60%. Let's look at the methods announced by the Shanghai Association. Chapter 2, wholesale rewards for the industry: elementary school textbooks and publications without copyrights, 80% to 75%; middle school textbooks, magazines, and other books, 85% to 80%; pre-ordered books, special-priced books, pre-ordered magazines, 90% to 85%. From this point, we know that the discounts between them are now smaller; in other words, the books of large bookstores such as Commercial Press that could previously be bought at 70% or 80% off in small bookstores now necessarily have to increase in price. At the same time, let's look at Article 4 of the Ministry of Education: "For published books, if the fixed price is higher due to the original discount, the respective publishers should immediately verify and reduce the price and set a real price..." Unfortunately, only Kaiming and New Life are responding to the Ministry's decree by automatically reducing book prices. Books of large bookstores like Commercial Press, which could previously be bought at 70% or 80% off (in small bookstores), now, after the methods issued by the Ministry (of course, these large bookstores have not reduced their prices), on the contrary, increase the burden on our general purchasers, and the price of books increases invisibly. This point cannot but make us suspect that Article 2 of the Ministry of Education stipulates: "The fixed price of textbooks should be based on the cost of editing and printing, appropriately determined, and strive to be low." Then, Commercial Press, China, World, and even Great East, and Beixin, which are famous for publishing textbooks, also seem to should slightly reduce their prices; otherwise, if they still sell at the previous 50% or 60% discount, it is known that they are not complying with the Ministry's order; or, they want to get through this summer vacation first and make some money first. Here, we cannot but say that the Shanghai Booksellers' Association's announcement on June 30th saying, "However, the ten articles of the Unified Book Sales Method issued by the Ministry of Education should be strictly followed by all our colleagues from this day forth; it is extremely important," is superfluous! It is vernacular! It is discussed but not implemented!

The Ministry of Education also knows that this method is not easy to implement; therefore, in Article 10, it is stipulated that if the rules are violated, local authorities can have considerable and effective sanctions; it is only a pity that the sanctions measures belonging to the local authorities have not been published. Although the Shanghai Booksellers' Association has specifically established Chapter 14 and stipulated four specific punishment methods, they have been postponed for some reason.

Now, it is not too late to mend the fold after the sheep is lost; I hope that the Ministry of Education may repeatedly order and declare to achieve success; at the same time, I hope that the Shanghai Association will not postpone it again after six months; and that booksellers in all regions will unite to break this long-standing malpractice in the publishing industry and achieve Mr. Duxiu's goal of "great flowering." That is not only a blessing for the publishing industry, but also dare to guarantee that the future of Chinese cultural undertakings will have the hope of development and glory.

Jane Eyre: An Autobiography 192

— Chen Youqin

Written by Englishwoman C. Brontë, translated by Li Jiye, published by Living Bookstore's World Literature Series

(I)

This "Jane Eyre: An Autobiography" is one of the famous long novels of the 19th century. I don't know if anyone in our country has translated it before. Recently, I continued reading from the fourth volume of the World Literature Series to the twelfth volume and finally appreciated this masterpiece. According to the World Literature Series edition, it is printed on more than 420 pages, and there is no separate edition yet. I am afraid that not many people have read this masterpiece, so I would like to briefly describe it as an introduction.

I think this is a very valuable and interesting book, although the author, Ms. Brontë, modestly calls it an unpretentious story. She became famous with this "Jane Eyre: An Autobiography," but the pen name she used at the time was Currer Bell, not Charlotte Brontë. As soon as the novel was published, it aroused the admiration of many readers, and everyone speculated about who this new author was, but Brontë never revealed her real name. She made the following statement in the third edition of the novel: "I want to use the opportunity of the third edition of 'Jane Eyre: An Autobiography' to say one more word to the readers and explain that I have the right to be called a novelist entirely because of this work. Therefore, if other novels are considered to be written by me, the honor will be given to the undeserving; as a result, the place where the honor should be given will not be received. This explanation can be used to correct the mistakes that have already been made and prevent future mistakes. April 13, 1848, Currer Bell." From her own remarks, it can be seen how important people at the time attached to this novel.

(II)

Regarding Ms. Brontë's life, the translator, Mr. Li Jiye, did not make an introduction, and readers probably don't know much about her, so I will specifically and briefly describe a few sentences below.

Brontë Charlotte is her real name. She was born in 1816 and died in 1855, living only 39 years.

She was the daughter of Reverend Brontë, who had the temperament of an Irishman and a naturally eccentric personality. His method of educating children was extremely special, often causing them to suffer a lot.

She was born in a small parsonage house close to the cemetery in a barren village of (HaworthParsonege), which cultivated her solitary nature. And in her childhood, she lost her kind mother. Because she was older, she had to take on the responsibility of her mother, taking care of and educating her two younger sisters. One was named Emily, and the other was named Anne, who eventually received her great help and also enjoyed a great reputation in the literary world. (These characters are quite relevant to the characterization of several supporting roles in "Jane Eyre: An Autobiography.")

After many efforts, she worked as a school teacher and a governess. Later, she and her sisters gathered funds to print some collections of poetry, signed as Currer, Ellis, or Acton, Bell. (This is slightly different from the pen name in "Jane Eyre: An Autobiography.") But the results were mediocre and did not receive much attention or welcome. (To be continued)

Written After the Closing of the World Jewish Congress 205

— Xiaoming

The World Jewish Congress has closed. Looking at the resolutions of the Congress, such as the protest against the expulsion of Jews by the German National Socialist Party, the request for the Soviet Union to allow Jews within its borders to freely practice Judaism, the request for all countries to stop prosecuting Jews participating in the movement to rebuild their homeland... etc., we can believe that the Jewish nation is excellent, at least not as inferior as the German Hitler's followers cursed.

What particularly highlights the heroism of the Jews is their severe resistance to the German National Socialist Party! They called on Jews around the world to boycott German goods as a response from the entire nation to the persecutors.

The Jews have always lacked the guarantee of their own national political power. They were not united and were subjected to discrimination by foreign races, which often led to innocent bullying. However, the spirit of this World Jewish Congress is sufficient to declare to the world, whether oppressors or sympathizers, the strength of the unity of the Jewish nation.

In Germany, since Hitler came to power, in order to expand its aggressive diplomacy externally and divert the public's attention from the social crisis internally, all the causes of Germany's poverty and weakness were blamed on the Jews. Hitler said in "Mein Kampf" that the destruction and wounds of Germany were entirely caused by the promiscuity of Jewish men and women, which disrupted the bloodline of the Germanic nation. Therefore, Hitler opposed Bolshevism and told German workers that Marx was a Jew. Hitler opposed science that revealed objective truth and said that Einstein was a Jew. Hitler banned films that satirized capitalism, also on the pretext that Charlie Chaplin was a Jew...

In short, the "anti-Jewish movement" has become a multifaceted tool for Hitler. Because it is a multifaceted tool, the damage is not limited to the Jews themselves, but extends to the entire world's lovers of freedom and culture.

Currently, this persecution of small ethnic groups and ethnic cultures is expanding. In Australia and the United States, Hitler's associates are also brewing anti-Jewish movements.

At this time, the convening of the World Jewish Congress is worthy of our excitement and sympathy. In the name of a similarly discriminated nation, we should express our respect to the courageous Jews and hope that they will firmly implement the resolutions of national self-defense after the closing of the conference. We believe that their actions can overcome the enemy's insults and win the support of the world's public who love cultural freedom.

In Hitler's writings, the Chinese nation is also a "degenerate race" and is ranked alongside pigs and dogs. If our nation is not even lower than the Jews, what should we express?

We should think about our position and the treatment of overseas Chinese!

The Homeless People 206

— Ai Tu

Since I came to Guangzhou, I always go to bed very late. It seems to be the inertia of my wandering nature. In every quiet late night, there are no pedestrians on the streets, only the familiar Dong Dong drumbeat of the watchman can be heard. A vast expanse of blue clouds covers the earth. At this time, I am very willing to drag my tired legs and limp to wander around. I do this until the fourth or fifth watch, and sometimes even until the rooster crows, before I quietly step onto the old building.

The summer nights in the South are so worthy of my lingering. Sometimes, I am simply like a human explorer, curiously observing everything in the dark streets. Because of this, I have been close to the many, many homeless people every night. However, these countless homeless people often occupy the entire sidewalk of the road. Sometimes, late at night, when I send Annie home, the countless shadows frighten them.

"Look, our doorway is blocked!" That fellow will definitely scold again when he sees it!"

If other women said this, I would definitely think that it contained endless resentment and boredom. But who would believe that Annie is the same as those noble ladies or young ladies? No! I can see from her tone that it contains endless sympathy and lament! Because I know that her life is close to these people. Although she also argues with the so-called upper-class young ladies sometimes, she is a daughter who has long hated everything in the current society.

Our doorway has been occupied by the homeless people, leaving only half a foot of space for us to enter and exit. One day, our landlord roared like an angry lion, calling the police to drive them away:

"No way! Sleeping at the door, looking like several corpses, is unsightly!"

He woke up the people who were sleeping soundly. We watched from behind with wide eyes and felt a little sad. When the landlord was gesturing so arrogantly, Annie sighed and said, "He was also born poor, a person without a home, raised by others, and becomes so arrogant when he gets rich?" But what else can we say? We watched with wide eyes as those people pleaded:

"Sir! Boss! We have no place to sleep!"

"Go somewhere else! Guangzhou is so big!"

"Other places are full of people! And it has rained, the ground is too wet! Look, the Song arcade is not a good place to sleep!"

"No way! My doorway is not your home! You are like corpses."

I saw these many innocent, ragged people walk away in anger.

In this way, I always saw countless homeless people on the streets. They had no clothes, were barefoot, and had naked legs. Every night, they occupied both sides of the road. They were hungry all day long, had no work, and writhed like countless insects in the corners. At night, they endured the wind and rain, gritting their teeth and letting the merciless mosquitoes suck their blood and flesh. But they couldn't even sleep happily!

I felt that the streets at night were filled with tragic shadows. We often saw the tragedy of the police driving away the homeless people for the landlord. Their fierce legs often frequented their bodies, especially when it rained, they were fighting for a place to sleep, searching in the dark corners like mice. But everywhere was already occupied by other people sleeping, so they would lower their heads and run to another place in disappointment.

When a new official took office, the first order issued, perhaps he thought it was the greatest miracle, the order meant this: "There are 20,000 displaced people in Guangzhou, who sleep on the streets every night, with bare arms and legs, which obstructs the view, and there are those who take the opportunity to disturb public order, which should be strictly prohibited..."

After this order was issued, the sticks of the police officers also became busy.

However, this huge whip, like a tiger, was applied to these 20,000 homeless people. Every night, isn't it still full of homeless people? One day, Annie said to me like this:

"It's really strange, why don't these officials understand that people have no place to sleep? Prohibition! Does the government have a place for them to sleep? Ha! It seems that they want them to die!"

I saw her shaking her head, but I didn't want to say anything. (Notes from Yangshi)

Exposed Corpse 207

— Xiu Yang

The exposed corpse was discovered by the water-carrier A Gen on the river beach.

Water-carrying in this town is an independent business. A Gen's grandfather relied on a special force to monopolize it, so his father and A Gen himself were named after their profession.

The shops and residents in this town rely on A Gen to deliver their daily water. Even those who are busy with their handicrafts also have to have A Gen carry a few loads of water.

At dawn, A Gen would jump out of bed, carry his water buckets that he depended on for survival to the river beach, and then deliver water door-to-door according to the distance. He would fill the water tanks for the shops and residents according to how much water they needed each day, and in addition, there were short-term businesses. He hardly had time to take a cigarette break the entire morning.

That day, he was carrying water buckets and singing mountain songs when he walked to the river beach. He saw a naked female corpse lying on the river beach. The corpse was already bloated, and the sky was not yet bright. A Gen was so frightened that he shouted.

Before long, many people had gathered around the river beach to watch the excitement. Some people also went to call the local constable to try to move the corpse ashore, covered the lower body with reeds, and asked someone the local constable had brought to knock on gongs in the streets and alleys, asking family members to come and identify the corpse.

Sure enough, more and more people came to watch the excitement, but no one came to identify the corpse. The corpse, roughly, had been soaked in the water for too long. The facial features had already rotted, and no one could guess who she was.

In the afternoon, the local constable went to the charitable hall to get a coffin and buried her in the public cemetery.

Here, the problem of drinking water arose. Everyone watched as a rotting corpse was carried ashore from the river. The shops and residents wanted A Gen to carry water from the big river ten miles away. A Gen naturally raised objections, saying:

"For ten copper coins a load of water, I have to run to the big river ten miles away. I can't earn a few hundred copper coins all day long. Who wants to do it! The corpse might have floated in from the big river. Isn't that a waste of effort?"

The users still firmly objected. They would rather not drink water. A Gen also angrily sent the water buckets home and went to the tavern.

The tavern was making this incident the news. The boss, the waiter, and the drinkers were all discussing it. When A Gen stepped into the tavern, because he was the one who discovered the corpse, everyone surrounded him and asked him questions.

A Gen couldn't do business today, and his stomach was full of grievances with no place to vent. He banged on the table and said, "Hmph, so excited about a female corpse. Do you want to fuck a dead woman?" He called the waiter to get wine, and then muttered to himself, "Let them go three days without drinking water!"

But the inexplicable corpse was too exciting. The drinkers were still privately discussing it, as if they were responsible for the investigation.

On this day, wherever two people in the town gathered, they were talking about this incident.

Until the lamps were lit, the local constable rushed into the tavern, pulled A Gen and said:

"The corpse has been identified. It's the wife of Official Chen. The police station wants you to question you."

A Gen was already slightly drunk. He grabbed the local constable and said, "Damn it, it's not my wife, ask what the bird!"

"Brother A Gen, that's not what I meant," the local constable always met resistance. He pleaded with A Gen, because you were the first to discover it, and they want you to be a witness. The town is already in a panic without water to drink, and the superiors are desperately trying to solve the case!"

A Gen laughed. He knew the power of his business. "Not drinking water, isn't not drinking water good for survival?" He grumbled and went to the police station with the local constable.

Official Chen had already fled. A Gen, with a lisp, told the police officer how he discovered the corpse. After the police station posted a wanted notice for the murderer, they only discussed the issue of the town's impending water shortage.

That was a murder case that occurred in the hometown in early spring. Official Chen has not been brought to justice to this day, and the people in the town no longer remember that sensational news. Every morning, the sound of A Gen's mountain song is singing again by the river beach.

Impressions of the Shanghai Orphanage (Part 1) 208

— Fang Zhou

(Special Report from This Newspaper) One new autumn afternoon, I boarded the public bus in Nanshi to Longhua to visit the Shanghai Orphanage.

The bus climbed up that long, wide cinder road, bumping very badly. The stench from the small muddy rivers drilled in through the car window in bursts, often making me cover my nose. The fields and houses on both sides flashed past like flying. We were getting further and further away from the city.

After getting off the bus in front of the Longhua Headquarters, I found the Shanghai Orphanage. Without notifying the gatekeeper, I went straight inside. It was an orchard, planted entirely with honey peach trees. Walking along a wide path in the middle, crossing a small bridge, it was another garden. Here there were also flowers, trees, pavilions, terraces, lawns, and rivers. Outside the garden was a row of tall willows, sheltering the sidewalk. At this time, several orphans were weeding by the side of the garden, laughing and playing, very lively.

Going in through a wooden fence gate, the outermost was the reception room; outside the room were placed two vats of lotus flowers and many other potted plants. We stood at the door of the room, wanting to find someone to report to the director here. At that time, an old nanny happened to come out from inside. I explained my intentions to her and gave her a business card. She took the business card, invited me into the reception room to sit for a while, and ordered a child to offer tea, and went next door to report.

The reception room was decorated very simply and elegantly. On the walls, in addition to many photos of the orphanage scenes and orphans' lives and work, there were also portraits of several deceased directors. There was also a photo of Mr. Shi Liangcai, the former owner of this newspaper, hanging on the wall, because Mr. Shi had donated 500 yuan to the orphanage's education fund.

While I was browsing the room, Director Zhang Jifu walked in. He was a kind and amiable old man. From his kind smile, we could see his character.

"Let's go next door to talk. It's quieter there," he said, gesturing for us to walk in front.

Haiyan Drama Society

Jiaotong (1300) 5:45 PM to 6:30 PM

Qian Liansheng...Bu Wei

Qian's Wife...Ming Jin, Her Daughter A Xiu...Mei Ying

Neighbor Auntie Li...Lu Lu

Her Daughter A Cai...Hui Ying

Sister A Qiao...Sun

Foreman Xu...Tan Guang

Bonded Laborer

Because of the oppression and exploitation of imperialism, the suffering of the Chinese working class and peasants is like the rising tide, drowning the workers and peasants so they cannot survive. Here, it exposes a realistic side of this corrupt old society - we heard every line and it seemed like we saw their dangerous and miserable expressions, and their dying struggles; and saw the cunning and vicious eyes of the traitors, and that bloody whip.

Here is the home of a plasterer. The plasterer, Qian Liansheng, builds Western-style buildings for those who exploit him every day, but he himself lives in a low, narrow thatched shed, living an inhuman life of not enough food and clothing. Now he has broken his arm while working and suffered a serious chest injury, but has been abandoned by the exploiters. He lies in bed, sickness and unemployment are the instruments of torture that could strangle him.

"Even if I recover, what's the use of having only one arm? Isn't it just waiting to starve to death?" he said sadly and angrily.

His wife accompanied him, her old tears streaming down her face. They thought of their daughter, A Xiu, waiting for Foreman Xu to pay the price for A Xiu's year as a bonded laborer – eight yuan – so they could buy medicine and see a doctor. However, they were afraid, worrying that A Xiu would be subjected to prison-like abuse. Because "bonded labor" means handing over the daughter to the foreman to work for three years, for a total price of thirty yuan, but during these three years the parents cannot see their daughter again, and the foreman is not responsible for her life or death. Therefore, the foreman can abuse the bonded laborers without any scruples, even more cruelly than slaves.

"Humph! Working hard like a beast for three hundred and sixty days a year, you only earn ten yuan. " The father only answered a smile to the mother's hope and consolation.

Indeed, the lives of laborers are only starvation, beatings, scolding, until they are exploited to death. Not only is this the case for plasterers and bonded laborers, but also for Auntie Li, the neighbor who sews sacks, who also came to say:

"Ever since the Japanese came and attacked Shanghai, everything is over! Before, we could earn more than thirty cents a day sewing sacks, and sometimes even more than forty cents! Now, well, we are so tired from sewing every day that we can't even earn twenty cents!" Then she revealed her sympathy for Qian Liansheng.

However, laborers living in this corrupt society can eat half full with twenty cents a day; but in these twenty cents, they have to pay for the thatched shed tax and all other kinds of expenses. Then the police can slap the daughter of the neighbor who cannot pay the thatched fence tax, and the neighbor runs home, preparing to be scolded.

And the female worker A Qiao came, her mouth full of gray sighs. She told the story of a bonded laborer who could not bear the hardship and hanged herself. This increased the mother's anxiety.

At this time, Qian Liansheng's daughter, A Xiu, ran back alone from the factory because she could not bear the abuse. She had a bad cold, dizziness, and a fever, but still had to work; today she really couldn't, she couldn't get out of bed, but the foreman still forced her to go to the night shift, and beat her, threatening her that if she didn't go to the night shift, he would take her life. So she ran home when she was dismissed from work.

From then on, life made the plasterer and the bonded laborer, as well as the kind mother, thoroughly understand this society.

But before the oppressed can unite into a vast force, Foreman Xu uses strong-arm tactics to drag his daughter A Xiu back to the hell-like factory. And he punched her father! Kicked over her mother!
